% Blueprint for "Fundamental Limitations on Subquadratic Alternatives to
% Transformers" (Josh Alman, Hantao Yu, ICLR 2025), arXiv:2410.04271v2.
%
% Two-kind model:
%   * LEAF nodes (\mathlibok, no proof) = standard facts already in Mathlib
%     (inner product, norm, continuity closure).
%   * FULL nodes = the paper's definitions, hypotheses, reductions, hardness
%     theorems and transformer constructions. These carry a complete statement,
%     \uses edges, and (for results) a complete proof. They are NOT marked
%     \leanok/\mathlibok.
% Node titles keep the paper's numbering, e.g. [Theorem 3.1], [Lemma A.8].

\chapter{Preliminaries: notation and library facts}

% --- Settled dependencies: already in Mathlib, emitted as leaves. -----------

\begin{definition}[Inner product of binary/real vectors]
  \label{def:inner-prod}
  \lean{inner}
  \mathlibok
  For $v, w \in \R^{\ell}$ we write $\inner{v}{w} = \sum_{i=1}^{\ell} v[i]\, w[i]$
  for their (standard) inner product, where $v[i]$ denotes the $i$-th entry of
  $v$. Equivalently, for vectors indexed by a finite type $I$, one may write
  $\inner{v}{w} = \sum_{i \in I} v_i w_i$. For binary vectors
  $v,w \in \{0,1\}^{\ell}$ this counts the coordinates on which both are $1$.
  Recalled only so later nodes can depend on it.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[$\ell_2$ norm]
  \label{def:l2norm}
  \lean{EuclideanSpace.norm_eq}
  \mathlibok
  For $v \in \R^{\ell}$, $\norm{v} = \sqrt{\inner{v}{v}}$ is the $\ell_2$ norm.
  We also use the $\ell_1$ norm $\norm{v}_1 = \sum_{i=1}^{\ell} |v[i]|$; for a
  binary vector $\norm{v}_1$ is its number of $1$ entries. Standard.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Kronecker (tensor) product of vectors]
  \label{def:kron}
  For finite index sets $I,J$, and vectors $v : I \to \R$ and $w : J \to \R$,
  the Kronecker product $v \otimes w : I \times J \to \R$ is the vector defined
  entrywise by
  \[
    (v \otimes w)_{(i,j)} = v_i w_j .
  \]
  For vectors in $\R^a$ and $\R^b$ this is the same vector in $\R^{ab}$ whose
  entries are all products of one entry of $v$ and one entry of $w$. This node
  defines only the binary Kronecker product. The $q$-fold Kronecker power
  notation is a separate concrete definition in
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power}.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Index type for $q$-fold Kronecker powers]
  \label{def:kron-power-index}
  For a finite index set $I$ and a natural number $q$, the coordinate index
  type of the $q$-fold Kronecker power is
  \[
    \operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q):=\mathrm{Fin}\,q\to I .
  \]
  Thus a coordinate is a choice of one original coordinate of $v$ for each of
  the $q$ tensor factors. This node defines only the index type. It does not
  define the vector entries, the zero-fold value, or the successor recursion.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Coordinate product for a Kronecker power]
  \label{def:kron-power-coordinate-product}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index}
  For a finite index set $I$, a vector $v:I\to\R$, a natural number $q$, and a
  coordinate $\sigma:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$, equivalently a
  function $\sigma:\mathrm{Fin}\,q\to I$, define the scalar
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPowerCoord}(v,q,\sigma)
      :=
      \prod_{r\in\mathrm{Fin}\,q} v_{\sigma(r)} .
  \]
  This node owns only the scalar product at one coordinate. It does not define
  the vector-valued Kronecker power and it does not state any base-case or
  successor behavior. A formal declaration at this label should be a single
  reducible definition of a scalar-valued function.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Vector-valued Kronecker power from coordinate products]
  \label{def:kron-power-vector}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-coordinate-product}
  For a finite index set $I$, a vector $v:I\to\R$, and a natural number $q$,
  define
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPowerVector}(v,q):
      \operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)\to\R
  \]
  by
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPowerVector}(v,q)(\sigma)
      :=
      \operatorname{kronPowerCoord}(v,q,\sigma).
  \]
  This node owns only the vector-valued function obtained by assembling the
  scalar coordinate products from
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-coordinate-product}. It should be formalized
  as one reducible definition and should not also prove the unfolded product
  formula.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Apply equation for the vector-valued Kronecker power]
  \label{lem:kron-power-apply}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-coordinate-product, def:kron-power-vector}
  For every finite index set $I$, vector $v:I\to\R$, natural number $q$, and
  coordinate $\sigma:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$,
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPowerVector}(v,q)(\sigma)
      =
      \prod_{r\in\mathrm{Fin}\,q} v_{\sigma(r)} .
  \]
  This node owns only the unfolded apply theorem. It is separated from
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-vector} so a formalization can prove the
  coordinate equation as one declaration, by unfolding
  Definitions~\ref{def:kron-power-vector} and
  \ref{def:kron-power-coordinate-product}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power-coordinate-product, def:kron-power-vector}
  Unfold the definition of $\operatorname{kronPowerVector}$, then unfold the
  scalar coordinate product from
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-coordinate-product}.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Public $q$-fold Kronecker power function]
  \label{def:kron-power-coordinate}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-coordinate-product, def:kron-power-vector, lem:kron-power-apply}
  For a finite index set $I$, a vector $v:I\to\R$, and a natural number $q$,
  define the public vector-valued function
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPower}(v,q):
      \operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)\to\R
  \]
  by the reducible alias
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPower}(v,q)
      :=\operatorname{kronPowerVector}(v,q).
  \]
  The unfolded coordinate product formula for this public name is supplied by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-apply}, after unfolding this alias.
  This label now owns only the public alias used by the rest of the blueprint.
  The scalar coordinate product, the vector assembly step, and the apply
  theorem are the separate helper nodes above. A formal declaration for this
  label must not package those three statements together as fields.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Zero-fold Kronecker power]
  \label{lem:kron-power-zero}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-coordinate, lem:kron-power-apply}
  For every finite index set $I$ and vector $v:I\to\R$, the zero-fold
  Kronecker power is the one-coordinate vector on
  $\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)$ and its unique coordinate has value $1$:
  \[
    \forall \sigma:\mathrm{Fin}\,0\to I,\qquad
    \operatorname{kronPower}(v,0)(\sigma)=1.
  \]
  Equivalently, under the unique equivalence
  $\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)\simeq \{\star\}$,
  $v^{\otimes0}$ is the constant one vector. This node is only the base case.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-coordinate, lem:kron-power-apply}
  Rewrite the public name $\operatorname{kronPower}$ by
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-coordinate}, then apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-apply}. The remaining product is over the empty
  finite type $\mathrm{Fin}\,0$, so it is the empty product, equal to $1$.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Successor-index rebracketing for Kronecker powers]
  \label{def:kron-power-succ-reindex}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index}
  For every finite index set $I$ and $q\in\N$, define the successor-coordinate
  rebracketing equivalence
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPowerSuccEquiv}_{I,q}:
      \operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q+1)
      \simeq I\times\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)
  \]
  by
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPowerSuccEquiv}_{I,q}(\sigma)
      =
      \bigl(\sigma(0),\, r\mapsto\sigma(r+1)\bigr).
  \]
  Its inverse sends $(i,\tau)$ to the coordinate
  $\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau):\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q+1)$
  defined by
  \[
    \operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(0)=i,\qquad
    \operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(r+1)=\tau(r)
    \quad(r:\mathrm{Fin}\,q).
  \]
  The declaration at this label owns only the equivalence, its inverse, and
  the two displayed coordinate equations. It does not state any product formula
  or equality of Kronecker-power vectors.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Head-tail product split over $\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)$]
  \label{lem:fin-succ-product-head-tail}
  For every natural number $q$ and every function
  $h:\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)\to\R$,
  \[
    \prod_{r\in\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)} h(r)
    =
    h(0)\cdot
    \prod_{r\in\mathrm{Fin}\,q} h(r+1).
  \]
  This node is only the generic finite-product reindexing that isolates the
  zero coordinate of $\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)$ and identifies the remaining
  coordinates with successors of coordinates of $\mathrm{Fin}\,q$. It does not
  mention Kronecker powers or successor coordinates.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  Split $\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)$ into the singleton coordinate $0$ and the image of
  the successor embedding $\mathrm{Fin}\,q\to\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)$. The two pieces
  are disjoint and exhaust $\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)$, so multiplicativity of finite
  products over disjoint unions gives the displayed equality. In Lean this is
  the single generic declaration to prove using the standard `Fin' successor
  product lemma or by finite-product congruence along the explicit equivalence
  $\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)\simeq \{\star\}\oplus\mathrm{Fin}\,q$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Head value of a successor Kronecker coordinate]
  \label{lem:kron-power-succ-coord-head}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-succ-reindex}
  For every finite index set $I$, $q\in\N$, $i:I$, and
  $\tau:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$,
  \[
    \operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(0)=i .
  \]
  This node owns only the zero-coordinate equation for the inverse of the
  successor-coordinate rebracketing equivalence.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power-succ-reindex}
  This is exactly the first defining coordinate equation for
  $\operatorname{succCoord}$ in
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-succ-reindex}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Finite-product congruence over a common index set]
  \label{lem:finite-product-pointwise-congr}
  \lean{Finset.prod_congr}
  \mathlibok
  For a finite index set $J$ and functions $f,g:J\to\R$, if
  $f(r)=g(r)$ for every $r:J$, then
  \[
    \prod_{r\in J} f(r)=\prod_{r\in J} g(r).
  \]
  This is the standard finite-product congruence lemma. It is isolated here so
  later Kronecker tail-product nodes only need to supply the pointwise equality
  of factors.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Tail coordinate of a successor Kronecker coordinate]
  \label{lem:kron-power-succ-coord-tail}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-succ-reindex}
  For every finite index set $I$, $q\in\N$, $i:I$,
  $\tau:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$, and $r:\mathrm{Fin}\,q$,
  \[
    \operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(r+1)=\tau(r).
  \]
  This node owns only the tail-coordinate equation for the inverse of the
  successor-coordinate rebracketing equivalence. It does not mention a vector
  $v$ and it does not form any product.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power-succ-reindex}
  This is exactly the second defining coordinate equation for
  $\operatorname{succCoord}$ in
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-succ-reindex}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Tail factor equality for successor Kronecker coordinates]
  \label{lem:kron-power-succ-tail-factor}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-succ-reindex, lem:kron-power-succ-coord-tail}
  For every finite index set $I$, vector $v:I\to\R$, $q\in\N$,
  $i:I$, $\tau:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$, and $r:\mathrm{Fin}\,q$,
  \[
    v_{\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(r+1)}
    =
    v_{\tau(r)}.
  \]
  This node owns only the pointwise equality of the two scalar factors that
  occur in the tail product. It is obtained by applying the vector $v$ to the
  coordinate equality of Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ-coord-tail}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-succ-coord-tail}
  Apply congruence of the function $v$ to
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ-coord-tail}. The resulting scalar equality is
  the displayed factor equality.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Tail product of a successor Kronecker coordinate]
  \label{lem:kron-power-succ-tail-product}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-succ-reindex, lem:finite-product-pointwise-congr, lem:kron-power-succ-tail-factor}
  For every finite index set $I$, vector $v:I\to\R$, $q\in\N$,
  $i:I$, and $\tau:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$,
  \[
    \prod_{r\in\mathrm{Fin}\,q}
      v_{\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(r+1)}
    =
    \prod_{r\in\mathrm{Fin}\,q}v_{\tau(r)}.
  \]
  This node is only the product-level composition step: apply finite-product
  congruence to the pointwise tail-factor equality of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ-tail-factor}. It does not prove the tail
  coordinate equation, it does not prove pointwise factor equality internally,
  it does not split the product over $\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)$, and it does not
  include the head factor $v_i$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:finite-product-pointwise-congr, lem:kron-power-succ-tail-factor}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-product-pointwise-congr} over the index set
  $\mathrm{Fin}\,q$ to the functions
  $r\mapsto v_{\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(r+1)}$ and
  $r\mapsto v_{\tau(r)}$. The required pointwise equality is exactly
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ-tail-factor}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Finite-product split for successor Kronecker coordinates]
  \label{lem:kron-power-succ-product-split}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-succ-reindex, lem:fin-succ-product-head-tail, lem:kron-power-succ-coord-head, lem:kron-power-succ-tail-product}
  For every finite index set $I$, vector $v:I\to\R$, $q\in\N$,
  $i:I$, and $\tau:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$,
  \[
    \prod_{r\in\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)}
      v_{\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(r)}
    =
      v_i\cdot
    \prod_{r\in\mathrm{Fin}\,q}v_{\tau(r)}.
  \]
  This node is now only the final composition of three smaller helper
  statements: the generic head-tail product split over $\mathrm{Fin}(q+1)$,
  the head-coordinate equation for $\operatorname{succCoord}$, and the tail
  product congruence. A formal declaration for this label should not reprove
  those helper statements internally.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:fin-succ-product-head-tail, lem:kron-power-succ-coord-head, lem:kron-power-succ-tail-product}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:fin-succ-product-head-tail} to the function
  $h(r)=v_{\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(r)}$. This rewrites the left-hand
  side as
  \[
    v_{\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(0)}\cdot
    \prod_{r\in\mathrm{Fin}\,q}
      v_{\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)(r+1)}.
  \]
  Rewrite the head factor by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ-coord-head} and rewrite the tail product by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ-tail-product}. The result is the displayed
  identity.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Successor apply equation for Kronecker powers]
  \label{lem:kron-power-succ-apply}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-coordinate, def:kron-power-succ-reindex, lem:kron-power-apply, lem:kron-power-succ-product-split}
  For every finite index set $I$, vector $v:I\to\R$, $q\in\N$,
  $i:I$, and $\tau:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$,
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPower}(v,q+1)
      \bigl(\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)\bigr)
    =
    v_i\cdot \operatorname{kronPower}(v,q)(\tau).
  \]
  This node owns only the coordinatewise successor equation for the public
  function $\operatorname{kronPower}$. It does not mention the binary
  Kronecker product $v\otimes\operatorname{kronPower}(v,q)$ and therefore does
  not package the final vector extensionality step.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power-coordinate, lem:kron-power-apply, lem:kron-power-succ-product-split}
  Rewrite both occurrences of the public name $\operatorname{kronPower}$ using
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-coordinate}. Apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-apply} to the $(q+1)$-fold and $q$-fold powers.
  The remaining scalar equality is exactly
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ-product-split}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Successor Kronecker power as a binary Kronecker product]
  \label{lem:kron-power-succ}
  \uses{def:kron, def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-coordinate, def:kron-power-succ-reindex, lem:kron-power-succ-apply}
  For a finite index set $I$, a vector $v:I\to\R$, and $q\in\N$, transport
  $\operatorname{kronPower}(v,q+1)$ along the successor-coordinate equivalence
  of Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-succ-reindex}.
  Under this equivalence, the successor Kronecker power is the binary
  Kronecker product of the first factor with the remaining $q$ factors:
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPower}(v,q+1)
    =
    v\otimes\operatorname{kronPower}(v,q).
  \]
  Equivalently, for every $i:I$ and
  $\tau:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$,
  \[
    \operatorname{kronPower}(v,q+1)
      \bigl(\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau)\bigr)
    =
    v_i\cdot \operatorname{kronPower}(v,q)(\tau).
  \]
  This node now owns only the final vector equality, proved from the successor
  apply equation and the binary Kronecker entry equation. The rebracketing
  equivalence, product split, and coordinatewise successor formula are the
  separate helper nodes above.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron, def:kron-power-succ-reindex, lem:kron-power-succ-apply}
  Prove equality of the transported vectors by extensionality on a coordinate
  $(i,\tau):I\times\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$. The left-hand side at
  this coordinate is
  $\operatorname{kronPower}(v,q+1)(\operatorname{succCoord}(i,\tau))$, which is
  $v_i\operatorname{kronPower}(v,q)(\tau)$ by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ-apply}. The right-hand side at $(i,\tau)$ is
  also $v_i\operatorname{kronPower}(v,q)(\tau)$ by
  Definition~\ref{def:kron}. Since all coordinates agree, the transported
  successor power equals
  $v\otimes\operatorname{kronPower}(v,q)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[$q$-fold Kronecker power notation]
  \label{def:kron-power}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-coordinate, lem:kron-power-apply, lem:kron-power-zero, def:kron-power-succ-reindex, lem:kron-power-succ-product-split, lem:kron-power-succ-apply, lem:kron-power-succ}
  The notation $v^{\otimes q}$ abbreviates the concrete vector
  $\operatorname{kronPower}(v,q)$ from
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-coordinate}, whose apply equation is
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-apply} and whose index type is
  $\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,q)$ from
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-index}. The base behavior is supplied by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero}, and the recursive binary-Kronecker behavior
  is supplied by Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ}.

  A formal declaration at this label is only a reducible alias or notation
  binding:
  \[
    v^{\otimes q}:=\operatorname{kronPower}(v,q).
  \]
  It must not restate the coordinate product definition, vector assembly
  definition, apply theorem, base case, and successor equation as fields of one
  large package. Those statements are the separate nodes above, each intended
  to correspond to one Lean declaration.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Finite sum over a product type]
  \label{lem:sum-prod-type}
  \lean{Fintype.sum_prod_type}
  \mathlibok
  For finite types $I,J$ and a function $h : I\times J \to \R$,
  \[
    \sum_{p\in I\times J} h(p)
    =
    \sum_{i\in I}\sum_{j\in J} h(i,j).
  \]
  This is the uncurried product-index expansion. In Lean, this is the
  unprimed theorem `Fintype.sum_prod_type`; the primed theorem is for a curried
  function and should not be used when the target is already a sum over
  $p : I\times J$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Product of two finite sums]
  \label{lem:sum-mul-sum}
  \lean{Fintype.sum_mul_sum}
  \mathlibok
  For finite types $I,J$ and functions $f : I\to\R$ and $g : J\to\R$,
  \[
    \left(\sum_{i\in I} f(i)\right)
    \left(\sum_{j\in J} g(j)\right)
    =
    \sum_{i\in I}\sum_{j\in J} f(i)g(j).
  \]
  Equivalently, the displayed double sum factors as the product of the two
  finite sums by using `Fintype.sum_mul_sum` in the reverse direction.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Finite-sum congruence over a common index set]
  \label{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr}
  \lean{Finset.sum_congr}
  \mathlibok
  For a finite index set $J$ and functions $f,g:J\to\R$, if
  $f(r)=g(r)$ for every $r:J$, then
  \[
    \sum_{r\in J} f(r)=\sum_{r\in J} g(r).
  \]
  This is the standard finite-sum congruence lemma. It is isolated so the
  Kronecker inner-product expansion only needs to provide the pointwise scalar
  equality of summands.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Scalar rearrangement for a Kronecker inner-product summand]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-summand-reassoc}
  For all real scalars $v,w,x,y$,
  \[
    (v x)(w y)=(v w)(x y).
  \]
  This node owns only the commutative-semiring normalization of one scalar
  summand. It does not mention finite sums, index products, inner products, or
  Kronecker products.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  Reassociate and commute the four factors in the commutative semiring $\R$:
  \[
    (v x)(w y)=v x w y=v w x y=(v w)(x y).
  \]
  A Lean proof should close this single scalar identity by the commutative
  semiring normalizer, e.g. `ring`, after unfolding no mathematical
  definitions.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Inner-product summand over an arbitrary finite index type]
  \label{def:inner-prod-index-summand}
  \uses{def:inner-prod}
  For a finite index set $K$, vectors $A,B:K\to\R$, and a coordinate $k:K$,
  define the scalar summand
  \[
    \operatorname{innerProdSummand}(A,B,k):=A_kB_k .
  \]
  This node owns only the pointwise scalar function used inside the finite sum
  for an inner product. It does not state any equality about $\inner{A}{B}$ and
  it does not specialize $K$ to a product type.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Apply equation for the inner-product summand]
  \label{lem:inner-prod-index-summand-apply}
  \uses{def:inner-prod-index-summand}
  For every finite index set $K$, vectors $A,B:K\to\R$, and coordinate $k:K$,
  \[
    \operatorname{innerProdSummand}(A,B,k)=A_kB_k .
  \]
  This node owns only the unfolded apply equation for the summand definition.
  It does not form a finite sum and it does not unfold the inner product.
  Trial-11 dependency-hygiene refinement: this node depends only on
  Definition~\ref{def:inner-prod-index-summand}. Downstream coordinate-sum
  definitions are not dependencies of this node, and any generated module for
  this node should import only the chunk containing
  `def_inner_prod_index_summand' (plus ordinary library imports). It must not
  import a later coordinate-sum chunk or any invalidated stale chunk merely
  because such a chunk was accepted in an earlier disposable run.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:inner-prod-index-summand}
  Unfold Definition~\ref{def:inner-prod-index-summand}. The resulting goal is
  the reflexive scalar equality
  \[
    A_kB_k=A_kB_k,
  \]
  so the formal proof must close immediately by reflexivity, for example
  `rfl' or `simpa [def_inner_prod_index_summand]'. It should not stop after
  the unfold step with an unsolved reflexive goal.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Coordinate-product finite-sum function]
  \label{def:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function}
  For a finite index set $K$ and vectors $A,B:K\to\R$, define the scalar
  function
  \[
    \operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}(A,B)
      :=
      \sum_{k\in K} A_kB_k .
  \]
  This node owns only the named finite-sum expression. It does not state that
  this sum is equal to $\inner{A}{B}$, and it does not introduce or use the
  auxiliary summand function
  $\operatorname{innerProdSummand}$. A formal declaration at this label should
  be one reducible definition of the scalar-valued function
  $\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}$.
  Trial-11 dependency-hygiene refinement: the audited declaration for this
  label has no blueprint-node dependency on
  Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-index-summand-apply}. It should compile from the
  finite-sum notation and the displayed formula alone. In particular, a
  generated chunk for `def_inner_prod_coordinate_sum_function' must not import
  the chunk for `lem_inner_prod_index_summand_apply' or any stale module that
  was invalidated by a later blueprint repair; importing that lemma would
  contradict the statement that this definition does not use the auxiliary
  summand function.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Apply equation for the coordinate-product finite-sum function]
  \label{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  \uses{def:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function}
  For every finite index set $K$ and vectors $A,B:K\to\R$,
  \[
    \operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}(A,B)
    =
    \sum_{k\in K} A_kB_k .
  \]
  This node owns only the unfolded apply equation for
  Definition~\ref{def:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function}. It does not mention
  $\operatorname{innerProdSummand}$ and it does not mention the inner product.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function}
  Unfold Definition~\ref{def:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function}. The
  remaining Lean goal is exactly
  \[
    \sum_{k\in K} A_kB_k=\sum_{k\in K} A_kB_k,
  \]
  and the proof of this node is complete only after closing that reflexive
  finite-sum equality by `rfl' or by
  `simpa [def_inner_prod_coordinate_sum_function]'. A generated proof that
  contains only
  `unfold def_inner_prod_coordinate_sum_function' is incomplete and does not
  satisfy this node, because it leaves the displayed reflexive equality as an
    unsolved goal.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Raw coordinate formula for finite inner products]
  \label{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum}
  \uses{def:inner-prod}
  For every finite index set $K$ and vectors $A,B:K\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{A}{B}
    =
    \sum_{k\in K} A_kB_k .
  \]
  This helper owns only the standard finite-coordinate formula for the inner
  product. It does not mention the named function
  $\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}$, the auxiliary summand function, product
  index types, or finite-sum congruence. A formal declaration at this label is
  therefore a single unfold/simp theorem for the coordinate formula of
  Definition~\ref{def:inner-prod}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:inner-prod}
  Unfold the finite-dimensional inner product from
  Definition~\ref{def:inner-prod}. The resulting expression is exactly the
  finite coordinate sum
  $\sum_{k\in K}A_kB_k$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Raw coordinate sum equals the named coordinate-sum function]
  \label{lem:raw-coordinate-sum-eq-coordinate-sum-function}
  \uses{def:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function, lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  For every finite index set $K$ and vectors $A,B:K\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{k\in K} A_kB_k
    =
    \operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}(A,B).
  \]
  This helper owns only the symmetric form of the apply equation for the named
  coordinate-sum function. It does not unfold the inner product and it does not
  prove any finite-sum congruence. A formal declaration at this label should
  use Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply} in reverse.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  Symmetrize Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply}, which
  states
  $\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}(A,B)=\sum_{k\in K}A_kB_k$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Inner product equals the named coordinate-sum function]
  \label{lem:inner-prod-eq-coordinate-sum-function}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum, lem:raw-coordinate-sum-eq-coordinate-sum-function}
  For every finite index set $K$ and vectors $A,B:K\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{A}{B}
    =
    \operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}(A,B).
  \]
  This node now owns only the final transitivity step from the raw coordinate
  formula to the named coordinate-sum function. It must not unfold
  $\inner{\cdot}{\cdot}$, unfold
  $\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}$, unfold the named summand, perform a
  finite-sum congruence, or specialize the index type. In Lean this should be a
  single declaration obtained by composing
  Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum} with
  Lemma~\ref{lem:raw-coordinate-sum-eq-coordinate-sum-function}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum, lem:raw-coordinate-sum-eq-coordinate-sum-function}
  First apply Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum}:
  \[
    \inner{A}{B}=\sum_{k\in K}A_kB_k .
  \]
  Then apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:raw-coordinate-sum-eq-coordinate-sum-function} to rewrite that
  raw finite sum as $\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}(A,B)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Inner product as the coordinate product sum]
  \label{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-unfold}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-eq-coordinate-sum-function, lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  For every finite index set $K$ and vectors $A,B:K\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{A}{B}
    =
    \sum_{k\in K} A_kB_k .
  \]
  This public node is now only the final transitivity step from
  Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-eq-coordinate-sum-function} and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply}. The definition of
  the named coordinate-sum function, its apply equation, the bridge from
  $\inner{A}{B}$ to that named function, and the final raw-sum rewrite are the
  separate helper nodes immediately above. A formal declaration at this label
  should not unfold the inner product internally.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-eq-coordinate-sum-function, lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  First apply Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-eq-coordinate-sum-function}:
  \[
    \inner{A}{B}=\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}(A,B).
  \]
  Then apply Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply} to
  rewrite the named coordinate-sum function as
  $\sum_{k\in K}A_kB_k$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Coordinate product sum as the named summand sum]
  \label{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-to-summand-sum}
  \uses{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr, lem:inner-prod-index-summand-apply}
  For every finite index set $K$ and vectors $A,B:K\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{k\in K} A_kB_k
    =
    \sum_{k\in K}\operatorname{innerProdSummand}(A,B,k).
  \]
  This node owns only the finite-sum congruence step from raw coordinate
  products to the named summand function. It does not unfold $\inner{A}{B}$ and
  it does not specialize the index type.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr, lem:inner-prod-index-summand-apply}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr} over the common index set
  $K$ to the functions $k\mapsto A_kB_k$ and
  $k\mapsto \operatorname{innerProdSummand}(A,B,k)$. At a coordinate $k$, the
  required equality is the symmetric form of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-index-summand-apply}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Inner product as the finite sum of its summands]
  \label{lem:inner-prod-index-sum-unfold}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-unfold, lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-to-summand-sum}
  For every finite index set $K$ and vectors $A,B:K\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{A}{B}
    =
    \sum_{k\in K}\operatorname{innerProdSummand}(A,B,k).
  \]
  This node now owns only the final transitivity step. The coordinate-sum
  formula for $\inner{A}{B}$ and the finite-sum congruence from coordinate
  products to named summands are the two separate helper lemmas immediately
  above. A formal declaration at this label should compose those helpers and
  should not unfold the inner product or prove the summand congruence
  internally.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-unfold, lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-to-summand-sum}
  First apply Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-unfold} to rewrite
  $\inner{A}{B}$ as $\sum_{k\in K}A_kB_k$. Then apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-to-summand-sum} to rewrite that
  coordinate-product sum as
  $\sum_{k\in K}\operatorname{innerProdSummand}(A,B,k)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Finite-sum expansion of inner-product summands]
  \label{lem:inner-prod-summand-sum-apply}
  \uses{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr, lem:inner-prod-index-summand-apply}
  For every finite index set $K$ and vectors $A,B:K\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{k\in K}\operatorname{innerProdSummand}(A,B,k)
    =
    \sum_{k\in K} A_kB_k .
  \]
  This node owns only the finite-sum congruence that replaces the named
  summand by its pointwise product formula. It does not unfold $\inner{A}{B}$
  and it does not mention product index types.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr, lem:inner-prod-index-summand-apply}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr} over the common index set
  $K$. At a coordinate $k$, the required equality is exactly
  Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-index-summand-apply}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Inner product expansion over a product index type]
  \label{lem:inner-prod-product-index-unfold}
  \uses{def:inner-prod-index-summand, lem:inner-prod-index-sum-unfold, lem:inner-prod-summand-sum-apply}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $A,B:I\times J\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{A}{B}
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J} A_p B_p .
  \]
  This node is only the specialization of the generic inner-product finite-sum
  unfolding to the product index type $I\times J$, followed by the separately
  formalized summand-apply finite-sum congruence. It does not define the
  summand, prove the generic finite-sum formula, or prove the pointwise
  summand equation internally. It also does not mention Kronecker products and
  it does not simplify any coordinate of $A$ or $B$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-index-sum-unfold, lem:inner-prod-summand-sum-apply}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-index-sum-unfold} with coordinate index
  $K=I\times J$ to rewrite
  \[
    \inner{A}{B}
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}\operatorname{innerProdSummand}(A,B,p).
  \]
  Then apply Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-summand-sum-apply}, again with
  $K=I\times J$, to unfold the named summand throughout the finite sum and
  obtain the displayed equality.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Pointwise Kronecker summand unfolding]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-coordinate-summand-unfold}
  \uses{def:kron}
  For finite index sets $I,J$, vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$, and a
  coordinate $p:I\times J$,
  \[
    (v\otimes x)_p\,(w\otimes y)_p
    =
    (v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  This node owns only the pointwise coordinate calculation for the two binary
  Kronecker products at one fixed product coordinate. It does not form a finite
  sum and it does not unfold the inner product.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron}
  By Definition~\ref{def:kron},
  $(v\otimes x)_p=v_{p_1}x_{p_2}$ and
  $(w\otimes y)_p=w_{p_1}y_{p_2}$. Substitute these two coordinate equations in
  the scalar product
  $(v\otimes x)_p(w\otimes y)_p$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Finite-sum Kronecker summand unfolding]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-coordinate-sum-unfold}
  \uses{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr, lem:kron-inner-coordinate-summand-unfold}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v\otimes x)_p\,(w\otimes y)_p
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  This node owns only the finite-sum congruence that lifts the pointwise
  Kronecker summand equation of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-coordinate-summand-unfold}. It does not unfold the
  inner product and it does not rearrange scalar factors.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr, lem:kron-inner-coordinate-summand-unfold}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr} over the common index set
  $I\times J$. The required pointwise equality at coordinate $p$ is exactly
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-coordinate-summand-unfold}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Unfolding a Kronecker inner product to a product-indexed sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-unfold-product-sum}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-product-index-unfold, lem:kron-inner-coordinate-sum-unfold}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  This node now owns only the composition of two smaller helper statements:
  first expand the inner product over the product index type, then lift the
  pointwise Kronecker coordinate equations through finite-sum congruence. It
  does not itself unfold either the inner product or the Kronecker product, it
  does not rearrange scalar factors, and it does not reindex the product-type
  sum as a double sum.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-product-index-unfold, lem:kron-inner-coordinate-sum-unfold}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-product-index-unfold} with
  $A=v\otimes x$ and $B=w\otimes y$ to obtain
  \[
    \inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}(v\otimes x)_p(w\otimes y)_p.
  \]
  Then apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-coordinate-sum-unfold} to rewrite this
  finite sum into the displayed product-indexed sum of unfolded Kronecker
  coordinates.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Pointwise reassociation under the product-indexed sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-product-sum-reassoc}
  \uses{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr, lem:kron-inner-summand-reassoc}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2})
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  This node owns only the finite-sum congruence step that rewrites each
  product-indexed summand into separated $I$- and $J$-factors. It does not
  unfold inner products or Kronecker products, and it does not convert the
  product-indexed sum into an iterated double sum.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr, lem:kron-inner-summand-reassoc}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-sum-pointwise-congr} over the common index set
  $I\times J$. For a fixed coordinate $p=(p_1,p_2)$, apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-summand-reassoc} with
  $v=v_{p_1}$, $x=x_{p_2}$, $w=w_{p_1}$, and $y=y_{p_2}$ to obtain
  \[
    (v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2})
    =
    (v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2}).
  \]
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Reindexing the separated product sum as a double sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-separated-product-sum-to-double}
  \uses{lem:sum-prod-type}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2})
    =
    \sum_{i\in I}\sum_{j\in J}(v_i w_i)(x_j y_j).
  \]
  This node owns only the product-index reindexing step for the already
  separated summand. It does not mention inner products or Kronecker products,
  and it does not perform scalar reassociation.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:sum-prod-type}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:sum-prod-type} to the function
  $h:I\times J\to\R$ defined by
  $h(p)=(v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2})$. The right-hand side is exactly the
  displayed iterated sum after writing $p=(i,j)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Raw product-indexed Kronecker inner-product sum]
  \label{def:kron-inner-raw-product-sum}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  define the scalar
  \[
    \operatorname{kronInnerRawProductSum}(v,w,x,y)
    :=
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  This node owns only the named raw product-indexed finite sum. It does not
  mention $\inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}$ and it does not reassociate any
  scalar factors. A formal declaration for this label should be one reducible
  definition of the displayed scalar-valued function.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Apply equation for the raw product-indexed Kronecker sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-raw-product-sum-apply}
  \uses{def:kron-inner-raw-product-sum}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \operatorname{kronInnerRawProductSum}(v,w,x,y)
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  This node owns only the unfolded apply equation for
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-inner-raw-product-sum}. It does not mention the
  Kronecker inner product and it does not reassociate scalar factors. A formal
  declaration at this label is a single unfold/`rfl' theorem: after unfolding
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-inner-raw-product-sum} the two sides are literally
  the same finite sum.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-inner-raw-product-sum}
  Unfold Definition~\ref{def:kron-inner-raw-product-sum}. The remaining Lean
  goal is the reflexive finite-sum equality
  \[
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}(v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2})
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}(v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2}),
  \]
  closed by `rfl' or `simpa [def_kron_inner_raw_product_sum]'. It must not be
  left as `:= sorry'.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Separated product-indexed Kronecker inner-product sum]
  \label{def:kron-inner-separated-product-sum}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  define the scalar
  \[
    \operatorname{kronInnerSeparatedProductSum}(v,w,x,y)
    :=
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  This node owns only the named separated product-indexed finite sum. It does
  not mention the Kronecker inner product, it does not prove equality with the
  raw sum, and it does not reindex the sum as an iterated double sum. A formal
  declaration for this label should be one reducible definition of the
  displayed scalar-valued function.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Apply equation for the separated product-indexed Kronecker sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-separated-product-sum-apply}
  \uses{def:kron-inner-separated-product-sum}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \operatorname{kronInnerSeparatedProductSum}(v,w,x,y)
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  This node owns only the unfolded apply equation for
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-inner-separated-product-sum}. It does not mention the
  Kronecker inner product and it does not reindex the sum as a double sum. A
  formal declaration at this label is a single unfold/`rfl' theorem.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-inner-separated-product-sum}
  Unfold Definition~\ref{def:kron-inner-separated-product-sum}; the remaining
  Lean goal is a reflexive finite-sum equality closed by `rfl' or
  `simpa [def_kron_inner_separated_product_sum]'. It must not be left as
  `:= sorry'.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Kronecker inner product equals the named raw product sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-eq-raw-product-sum}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-unfold-product-sum, lem:kron-inner-raw-product-sum-apply}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}
    =
    \operatorname{kronInnerRawProductSum}(v,w,x,y).
  \]
  This node owns only the naming step from the already formalized
  product-indexed unfolding to the raw sum definition. It does not perform the
  pointwise Kronecker-coordinate calculation internally, and it does not
  reassociate scalar factors.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-unfold-product-sum, lem:kron-inner-raw-product-sum-apply}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-unfold-product-sum} to rewrite the
  Kronecker inner product as
  \[
    \sum_{p\in I\times J} (v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  Then rewrite this finite sum as
  $\operatorname{kronInnerRawProductSum}(v,w,x,y)$ using the reverse direction
  of Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-raw-product-sum-apply}.

  Both steps are explicit lemma rewrites, not definitional closures. In Lean,
  `rw [kron_inner_unfold_product_sum]` puts the goal in the finite-sum form and
  `rw [\leftarrow kron_inner_raw_product_sum_apply]` (or
  `exact (kron_inner_raw_product_sum_apply ..).symm.trans ...`) rewrites the sum
  to the named function. The generated declaration must carry out these two
  rewrites and must not be left as `:= sorry'; an admitted placeholder does not
  certify the equality even though it type-checks.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Named raw product sum equals the named separated product sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-raw-eq-separated-product-sum}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-raw-product-sum-apply, lem:kron-inner-separated-product-sum-apply, lem:kron-inner-product-sum-reassoc}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \operatorname{kronInnerRawProductSum}(v,w,x,y)
    =
    \operatorname{kronInnerSeparatedProductSum}(v,w,x,y).
  \]
  This node owns only the naming step around the already formalized finite-sum
  reassociation. It does not unfold the Kronecker inner product, it does not
  prove the scalar reassociation internally, and it does not reindex the
  product-indexed sum as a double sum.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-raw-product-sum-apply, lem:kron-inner-separated-product-sum-apply, lem:kron-inner-product-sum-reassoc}
  Rewrite the left-hand side by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-raw-product-sum-apply}:
  \[
    \operatorname{kronInnerRawProductSum}(v,w,x,y)
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}(v_{p_1}x_{p_2})(w_{p_1}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  Rewrite this finite sum by Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-product-sum-reassoc} to
  obtain $\sum_{p\in I\times J}(v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2})$. Finally
  rewrite by the reverse direction of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-separated-product-sum-apply} to reach
  $\operatorname{kronInnerSeparatedProductSum}(v,w,x,y)$.

  Each of the three steps is an explicit lemma rewrite. In Lean,
  `rw [kron_inner_raw_product_sum_apply, kron_inner_product_sum_reassoc,
  \leftarrow kron_inner_separated_product_sum_apply]` discharges the goal. The
  generated declaration must actually invoke these dependencies and must not be
  left as `:= sorry'.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Kronecker inner product after summand reassociation]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-product-sum}
  \uses{def:kron-inner-separated-product-sum, lem:kron-inner-eq-raw-product-sum, lem:kron-inner-raw-eq-separated-product-sum}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}
    =
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  This helper now owns only the final public restatement of two smaller
  naming lemmas. Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-eq-raw-product-sum} rewrites the
  Kronecker inner product to the named raw product sum, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-raw-eq-separated-product-sum} rewrites that named
  raw sum to the named separated product sum. This node then unfolds only
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-inner-separated-product-sum} to display the
  separated finite sum. It does not inspect the product-indexed unfolding,
  prove scalar reassociation, reindex as a double sum, or factor the double
  sum.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-inner-separated-product-sum, lem:kron-inner-eq-raw-product-sum, lem:kron-inner-raw-eq-separated-product-sum}
  First apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-eq-raw-product-sum}:
  \[
    \inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}
    =
    \operatorname{kronInnerRawProductSum}(v,w,x,y).
  \]
  Then apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-raw-eq-separated-product-sum} to obtain
  \[
    \inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}
    =
    \operatorname{kronInnerSeparatedProductSum}(v,w,x,y).
  \]
  Finally unfold Definition~\ref{def:kron-inner-separated-product-sum}; the
  right-hand side becomes exactly the displayed separated product-indexed sum.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Reassociated Kronecker product-index sum as a double sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-to-double}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-separated-product-sum-to-double}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{p\in I\times J}
      (v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2})
    =
    \sum_{i\in I}\sum_{j\in J}(v_i w_i)(x_j y_j).
  \]
  This helper owns only the second transitivity step in the expansion of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-expanded-double-sum}. It is a public alias for the
  reindexing statement that the final expanded-double-sum node needs, so that
  the final node does not need to inspect the product-index reindexing proof.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-separated-product-sum-to-double}
  This is exactly
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-separated-product-sum-to-double}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Expanded Kronecker inner product as a factored double sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-expanded-double-sum}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-product-sum, lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-to-double}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}
    =
    \sum_{i\in I}\sum_{j\in J}(v_i w_i)(x_j y_j).
  \]
  This node is now only the final transitivity step between two explicit
  helper statements. Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-product-sum}
  rewrites the Kronecker inner product to the separated product-indexed sum,
  and Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-to-double} reindexes that
  exact separated sum as the displayed double sum. A formal declaration at this
  label should compose those two equations only. It must not unfold
  definitions, prove pointwise scalar rearrangement, inspect the product-index
  reindexing proof, or factor the double sum as a product of two sums.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-product-sum, lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-to-double}
  First apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-product-sum}:
  \[
    \sum_{p\in I\times J} (v_{p_1}w_{p_1})(x_{p_2}y_{p_2}).
  \]
  Finally apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-to-double} to this exact
  separated product-indexed sum to obtain the displayed iterated double sum.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Separated double sum as a product of coordinate sums]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-double-sum-to-product}
  \uses{lem:sum-mul-sum}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{i\in I}\sum_{j\in J}(v_i w_i)(x_j y_j)
    =
    \left(\sum_{i\in I} v_i w_i\right)\left(\sum_{j\in J} x_j y_j\right).
  \]
  This node owns only the single finite-sum factorization step. It does not
  mention inner products or Kronecker products, and it does not identify either
  coordinate sum with an inner product. In Lean it is one reverse rewrite by
  `Fintype.sum_mul_sum'.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:sum-mul-sum}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:sum-mul-sum} in the reverse direction with
  $f(i)=v_iw_i$ and $g(j)=x_jy_j$. The single Lean step is
  `rw [\leftarrow Fintype.sum_mul_sum]' (or `exact (Fintype.sum_mul_sum ..).symm').
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Product of coordinate sums equals the product of inner products]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-product-of-sums-eq-inner}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \left(\sum_{i\in I} v_i w_i\right)\left(\sum_{j\in J} x_j y_j\right)
    =
    \inner{v}{w}\cdot\inner{x}{y}.
  \]
  This node owns only the identification of each raw coordinate sum with an
  inner product, using Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum} in
  reverse. It performs no finite-sum factorization and mentions no Kronecker
  product. The identification of $\sum_i v_iw_i$ with $\inner{v}{w}$ is
  \emph{not} definitional for the Mathlib inner product on Euclidean space; it
  must be discharged by Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum} and it
  cannot be closed by `rfl'.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum}
  By Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-eq-raw-coordinate-sum}, applied in reverse with
  $K=I$ and then with $K=J$,
  \[
    \sum_{i\in I} v_i w_i=\inner{v}{w},
    \qquad
    \sum_{j\in J} x_j y_j=\inner{x}{y}.
  \]
  Rewrite both factors accordingly; the Lean step is
  `rw [\leftarrow inner_prod_eq_raw_coordinate_sum,
  \leftarrow inner_prod_eq_raw_coordinate_sum]'. It must not be left as `sorry'.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Factoring the Kronecker inner-product double sum]
  \label{lem:kron-inner-double-sum-factor}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-double-sum-to-product, lem:kron-inner-product-of-sums-eq-inner}
  For finite index sets $I,J$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$ and $x,y:J\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{i\in I}\sum_{j\in J}(v_i w_i)(x_j y_j)
    =
    \inner{v}{w}\cdot\inner{x}{y}.
  \]
  This node is now only the final transitivity step between two separately
  formalized helpers. Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-double-sum-to-product} rewrites
  the double sum as the product of two coordinate sums, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-product-of-sums-eq-inner} identifies that product
  with $\inner{v}{w}\cdot\inner{x}{y}$. A formal declaration at this label
  composes those two equations and must not perform the finite-sum
  factorization or the inner-product identification internally.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-double-sum-to-product, lem:kron-inner-product-of-sums-eq-inner}
  First apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-double-sum-to-product} to rewrite the
  double sum as
  $\left(\sum_{i\in I} v_i w_i\right)\left(\sum_{j\in J} x_j y_j\right)$. Then
  apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-product-of-sums-eq-inner} to identify this
  product with $\inner{v}{w}\cdot\inner{x}{y}$. In Lean this is
  `rw [kron_inner_double_sum_to_product, kron_inner_product_of_sums_eq_inner]'.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Multiplicativity of inner products under Kronecker product]
  \label{lem:kron-inner}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:kron, lem:kron-inner-expanded-double-sum, lem:kron-inner-double-sum-factor}
  For $v,w \in \R^{a}$ and $x,y\in\R^{b}$,
  \[
    \inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}
    =
    \inner{v}{w}\cdot\inner{x}{y}.
  \]
  This node is only the binary Kronecker identity. The $q$-fold consequences
  used in Appendix B are separate nodes
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner}, Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-norm}, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-cosine}. The scalar rearrangement, product-index
  expansion, and finite-sum factorization used to prove this identity are the
  separate helper nodes
  Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-product-index-unfold},
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-coordinate-summand-unfold},
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-coordinate-sum-unfold},
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-summand-reassoc},
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-unfold-product-sum},
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-product-sum-reassoc},
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-separated-product-sum-to-double},
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-product-sum},
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-expanded-reassociated-to-double},
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-expanded-double-sum}, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-double-sum-factor}. A formal declaration at this
  label should therefore only compose those helpers; it should not reprove the
  scalar normalization, the product-type reindexing, or the double-sum
  factorization internally.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-inner-expanded-double-sum, lem:kron-inner-double-sum-factor}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-expanded-double-sum} to rewrite
  $\inner{v\otimes x}{w\otimes y}$ as
  \[
    \sum_{i\in I}\sum_{j\in J}(v_i w_i)(x_j y_j).
  \]
  Then apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner-double-sum-factor} to identify this
  double sum with $\inner{v}{w}\cdot\inner{x}{y}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Empty coordinate of the zero-fold Kronecker index]
  \label{def:kron-power-zero-coordinate}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index}
  For every finite index set $I$, define
  \[
    \operatorname{emptyKronCoord}_I:
      \operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)
  \]
  to be the unique function $\mathrm{Fin}\,0\to I$. This node owns only the
  canonical coordinate of the zero-fold Kronecker index type. It does not state
  uniqueness, any Kronecker-power value equation, or any inner-product
  calculation.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Uniqueness of the zero-fold Kronecker coordinate]
  \label{lem:kron-power-zero-index-singleton}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-zero-coordinate}
  For every finite index set $I$ and every
  $\sigma:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)$,
  \[
    \sigma=\operatorname{emptyKronCoord}_I .
  \]
  Thus the index type $\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)$ has exactly one
  coordinate. This node owns only the function-extensionality fact for
  functions out of $\mathrm{Fin}\,0$; it does not evaluate
  $v^{\otimes0}$ and it does not form a finite sum.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index, def:kron-power-zero-coordinate}
  Prove equality of functions $\sigma,\operatorname{emptyKronCoord}_I:
  \mathrm{Fin}\,0\to I$ by extensionality. There is no coordinate
  $r:\mathrm{Fin}\,0$, so the pointwise goal has no cases.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Real scalar one times one]
  \label{lem:real-one-mul-one}
  \lean{mul_one}
  \mathlibok
  In the real numbers,
  \[
    1\cdot1=1.
  \]
  This is a settled scalar normalization fact. It is isolated so proofs that
  first rewrite both factors of a product to $1$ have an explicit final
  dependency for the residual goal $1*1=1$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Zero-fold Kronecker inner-product summand]
  \label{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-summand}
  \uses{def:kron-power, lem:kron-power-zero, lem:real-one-mul-one}
  For every finite index set $I$, vectors $v,w:I\to\R$, and
  $\sigma:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)$,
  \[
    v^{\otimes0}(\sigma)\,w^{\otimes0}(\sigma)=1 .
  \]
  This node owns the full zero-fold summand evaluation as a single declaration.
  It rewrites each coordinate factor to $1$ using
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero} and then closes the residual scalar identity
  $1\cdot1=1$ by Lemma~\ref{lem:real-one-mul-one}. It does not use
  singleton-ness of the index type and it does not expand the inner product.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power, lem:kron-power-zero, lem:real-one-mul-one}
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero} gives $v^{\otimes0}(\sigma)=1$ and
  $w^{\otimes0}(\sigma)=1$. Rewrite the two coordinate factors by these
  equations; the goal becomes the scalar identity $1\cdot1=1$, which is closed
  by Lemma~\ref{lem:real-one-mul-one}. In Lean,
  `rw [kron_power_zero, kron_power_zero]; exact real_one_mul_one' (or
  `simp [kron_power_zero]'). It must not be left as `:= sorry'.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Zero-fold Kronecker inner-sum index type]
  \label{def:kron-power-zero-inner-index}
  \uses{def:kron-power-index}
  For every finite index set $I$, define the index type used by the zero-fold
  Kronecker inner-coordinate sum to be
  \[
    \operatorname{ZeroKronInnerIndex}(I)
      :=\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0).
  \]
  This node owns only the specialized index-type alias. It does not construct
  either argument vector and it does not apply any coordinate-sum function.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Left zero-fold Kronecker argument for the inner-coordinate sum]
  \label{def:kron-power-zero-inner-left-arg}
  \uses{def:kron-power, def:kron-power-zero-inner-index}
  For every finite index set $I$ and vector $v:I\to\R$, define
  \[
    \operatorname{zeroKronInnerLeftArg}(v):
      \operatorname{ZeroKronInnerIndex}(I)\to\R
  \]
  by the reducible alias
  \[
    \operatorname{zeroKronInnerLeftArg}(v):=v^{\otimes0}.
  \]
  This node owns only the first argument supplied to the generic coordinate-sum
  function. It does not mention the second vector $w$ and it does not define
  $\operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Right zero-fold Kronecker argument for the inner-coordinate sum]
  \label{def:kron-power-zero-inner-right-arg}
  \uses{def:kron-power, def:kron-power-zero-inner-index}
  For every finite index set $I$ and vector $w:I\to\R$, define
  \[
    \operatorname{zeroKronInnerRightArg}(w):
      \operatorname{ZeroKronInnerIndex}(I)\to\R
  \]
  by the reducible alias
  \[
    \operatorname{zeroKronInnerRightArg}(w):=w^{\otimes0}.
  \]
  This node owns only the second argument supplied to the generic
  coordinate-sum function. It does not mention the first vector $v$ and it does
  not define $\operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Named zero-fold Kronecker inner coordinate sum]
  \label{def:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function}
  \uses{def:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function, def:kron-power-zero-inner-index, def:kron-power-zero-inner-left-arg, def:kron-power-zero-inner-right-arg}
  For every finite index set $I$ and vectors $v,w:I\to\R$, define the scalar
  function
  \[
    \operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}(v,w)
      :=
      \operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}
        \bigl(\operatorname{zeroKronInnerLeftArg}(v),
              \operatorname{zeroKronInnerRightArg}(w)\bigr).
  \]
  The two arguments are the separate aliases from
  Definitions~\ref{def:kron-power-zero-inner-left-arg} and
  \ref{def:kron-power-zero-inner-right-arg}, both over the specialized index
  type of Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-zero-inner-index}. This node owns only
  the final application of
  $\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}$ to those two already-defined arguments. It
  does not unfold either Kronecker power, define the index type, unfold the
  inner product, or expand the generic coordinate-sum function to a finite sum.
  A formal declaration at this label should be one reducible definition of
  $\operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}$ whose right-hand side is exactly the
  displayed application to the two helper argument functions.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Zero-fold Kronecker inner product equals the named coordinate sum]
  \label{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-coordinate-sum-function}
  \uses{def:kron-power, def:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function, lem:inner-prod-eq-coordinate-sum-function}
  For every finite index set $I$ and every $v,w:I\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{v^{\otimes0}}{w^{\otimes0}}
    =
    \operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}(v,w).
  \]
  This helper owns only the specialization of the generic theorem
  $\inner{A}{B}=\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}(A,B)$ to
  $A=v^{\otimes0}$ and $B=w^{\otimes0}$, followed by the naming definition
  above. It does not unfold
  $\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}$ to a raw finite sum and it does not prove
  any fact about the zero-fold index type.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function, lem:inner-prod-eq-coordinate-sum-function}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-eq-coordinate-sum-function} with
  $K=\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)$,
  $A=v^{\otimes0}$, and $B=w^{\otimes0}$. The right-hand side is exactly
  $\operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}(v,w)$ by
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Named zero-fold Kronecker inner coordinate sum unfolds]
  \label{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  \uses{def:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function, lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  For every finite index set $I$ and every $v,w:I\to\R$,
  \[
    \operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}(v,w)
    =
    \sum_{\sigma\in\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)}
      v^{\otimes0}(\sigma)\,w^{\otimes0}(\sigma).
  \]
  This helper owns only the apply theorem for the named zero-fold coordinate
  sum. It unfolds
  $\operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}$ to the generic
  $\operatorname{innerProdCoordSum}$ and then uses the generic apply theorem
  for that function. It does not mention the inner product.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function, lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  Unfold
  Definition~\ref{def:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function}. Then
  apply Lemma~\ref{lem:inner-prod-coordinate-sum-function-apply} to
  $A=v^{\otimes0}$ and $B=w^{\otimes0}$ over the index type
  $\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Zero-fold Kronecker inner product as a coordinate sum]
  \label{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-coordinate-sum-function, lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  For every finite index set $I$ and every $v,w:I\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{v^{\otimes0}}{w^{\otimes0}}
    =
    \sum_{\sigma\in\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)}
      v^{\otimes0}(\sigma)\,w^{\otimes0}(\sigma).
  \]
  This node is now only the final transitivity step. The inner product is first
  rewritten to the named scalar
  $\operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}(v,w)$ by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-coordinate-sum-function}, and that
  named scalar is then unfolded to the displayed finite sum by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function-apply}. It does
  not specialize the generic inner-product expansion internally and it does not
  unfold the coordinate-sum function internally.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-coordinate-sum-function, lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function-apply}
  First rewrite
  $\inner{v^{\otimes0}}{w^{\otimes0}}$ as
  $\operatorname{zeroKronInnerCoordSum}(v,w)$ by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-coordinate-sum-function}. Then apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-function-apply} to
  rewrite the named scalar as the displayed finite sum.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Finite sum over the zero-fold Kronecker index]
  \label{lem:kron-power-zero-index-sum}
  \uses{def:kron-power-zero-coordinate, lem:kron-power-zero-index-singleton}
  For every finite index set $I$ and every function
  $f:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{\sigma\in\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)} f(\sigma)
    =
    f(\operatorname{emptyKronCoord}_I).
  \]
  This helper owns only the singleton finite-sum collapse for the zero-fold
  Kronecker index. It is independent of inner products and independent of
  Kronecker-power coordinate values.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:kron-power-zero-coordinate, lem:kron-power-zero-index-singleton}
  By Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-index-singleton}, every
  $\sigma:\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)$ is equal to
  $\operatorname{emptyKronCoord}_I$. Therefore the finite sum over this
  singleton index type is exactly the value of $f$ at
  $\operatorname{emptyKronCoord}_I$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Coordinate sum of zero-fold Kronecker inner summands is one]
  \label{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-eq-one}
  \uses{def:kron-power-zero-coordinate, lem:kron-power-zero-index-sum, lem:kron-power-zero-inner-summand}
  For every finite index set $I$ and every $v,w:I\to\R$,
  \[
    \sum_{\sigma\in\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)}
      v^{\otimes0}(\sigma)\,w^{\otimes0}(\sigma)
    =
    1 .
  \]
  This helper owns only the final value of the already-expanded coordinate
  sum. It collapses the sum to the canonical zero-fold coordinate and then
  applies the pointwise summand lemma. It does not unfold the inner product.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-zero-index-sum, lem:kron-power-zero-inner-summand}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-index-sum} to the function
  \[
    \sigma\mapsto v^{\otimes0}(\sigma)\,w^{\otimes0}(\sigma).
  \]
  This rewrites the finite sum as
  $v^{\otimes0}(\operatorname{emptyKronCoord}_I)\,
   w^{\otimes0}(\operatorname{emptyKronCoord}_I)$, which is $1$ by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-summand}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Inner product of two zero-fold Kronecker powers is one]
  \label{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-one}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum, lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-eq-one}
  For every finite index set $I$ and every $v,w:I\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{v^{\otimes0}}{w^{\otimes0}}=1 .
  \]
  This node now owns only the final transitivity step. The inner-product
  expansion is Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum}, and the
  value of that coordinate sum is
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-eq-one}. A formal
  declaration for this label must not unfold the inner product, prove
  singleton-ness of $\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}(I,0)$, or evaluate the
  zero-fold summand internally.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum, lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-eq-one}
  First rewrite
  $\inner{v^{\otimes0}}{w^{\otimes0}}$ as the coordinate sum by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum}. Then rewrite that
  coordinate sum to $1$ by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-coordinate-sum-eq-one}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Base case for inner products of Kronecker powers]
  \label{lem:kron-power-inner-zero}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-one}
  For every finite index set $I$ and every $v,w:I\to\R$,
  \[
    \inner{v^{\otimes0}}{w^{\otimes0}}=\inner{v}{w}^{0}.
  \]
  This node now owns only the final base-case equality. The finite
  inner-product computation on the zero-fold singleton index is
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-one}; the only remaining scalar fact
  is the standard identity $x^0=1$. A formal declaration at this label should
  compose those two one-line facts and must not unfold
  $\operatorname{KronPowerIndex}$, prove uniqueness of the empty coordinate,
  evaluate zero-fold Kronecker coordinates, or expand the inner product.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-one}
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-zero-inner-eq-one} rewrites the left-hand side as
  $1$. The scalar power identity rewrites $\inner{v}{w}^{0}$ as $1$. The
  desired equality follows by transitivity.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Successor inner product before applying the induction hypothesis]
  \label{lem:kron-power-inner-succ-mul}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:kron-power, lem:kron-power-succ, lem:kron-inner}
  For every finite index set $I$, every $v,w:I\to\R$, and every natural $q$,
  after transporting the $(q+1)$-fold powers along the successor-coordinate
  equivalence,
  \[
    \inner{v^{\otimes(q+1)}}{w^{\otimes(q+1)}}
    =
    \inner{v}{w}\cdot
    \inner{v^{\otimes q}}{w^{\otimes q}}.
  \]
  This node owns only the successor reduction to the binary Kronecker identity.
  It does not use or state the induction hypothesis, and it does not simplify
  scalar powers. A formal declaration for this label should compose
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ} for $v$ and $w$ with
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-succ, lem:kron-inner}
  Under the successor-coordinate equivalence of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-succ},
  \[
    v^{\otimes(q+1)}=v\otimes v^{\otimes q},
    \qquad
    w^{\otimes(q+1)}=w\otimes w^{\otimes q}.
  \]
  Substitute these two vector equalities into the left-hand side and then apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-inner}. The result is exactly
  $\inner{v}{w}\cdot\inner{v^{\otimes q}}{w^{\otimes q}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Successor inner product after applying the induction hypothesis]
  \label{lem:kron-power-inner-succ-step}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-inner-succ-mul}
  For every finite index set $I$, every $v,w:I\to\R$, and every natural $q$, if
  \[
    \inner{v^{\otimes q}}{w^{\otimes q}}=\inner{v}{w}^{q},
  \]
  then
  \[
    \inner{v^{\otimes(q+1)}}{w^{\otimes(q+1)}}
    =
    \inner{v}{w}^{q+1}.
  \]
  This node owns only the induction-step implication. It assumes the
  $q$-fold identity as a hypothesis, uses
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner-succ-mul} to expose the multiplicative
  successor form, substitutes the hypothesis, and closes the scalar equality by
  the standard successor-power equation. It does not reprove the binary
  Kronecker inner-product identity or the successor rebracketing.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-inner-succ-mul}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner-succ-mul} to rewrite the successor
  inner product as
  \[
    \inner{v}{w}\cdot\inner{v^{\otimes q}}{w^{\otimes q}}.
  \]
  Substitute the displayed induction hypothesis. The remaining scalar identity
  is
  \[
    \inner{v}{w}\cdot\inner{v}{w}^{q}
    =
    \inner{v}{w}^{q+1},
  \]
  which is exactly the successor equation for powers in the commutative
  semiring $\R$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Inner products of Kronecker powers]
  \label{lem:kron-power-inner}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:kron-power, lem:kron-power-inner-zero, lem:kron-power-inner-succ-step}
  For every finite index set $I$, every $v,w:I\to\R$, and every natural
  $q$, where $v^{\otimes q}$ and $w^{\otimes q}$ are indexed by functions
  $\{1,\ldots,q\}\to I$,
  \[
    \inner{v^{\otimes q}}{w^{\otimes q}}=\inner{v}{w}^{q}.
  \]
  The formal statement must specify the indexing convention for the $q$-fold
  power, for example the index type $\mathrm{Fin}\,q\to I$ with the empty
  product equal to $1$ when $q=0$. This public node is now only the induction
  wrapper: its base case is Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner-zero}, and its
  successor step is Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner-succ-step}. It must not
  unfold the coordinate products, reprove successor rebracketing, invoke the
  binary Kronecker inner-product calculation directly, or perform the scalar
  power simplification internally.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-inner-zero, lem:kron-power-inner-succ-step}
  Induct on $q$. The base case is
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner-zero}. For the successor step, apply
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner-succ-step} to the induction hypothesis.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Euclidean norms of Kronecker powers]
  \label{lem:kron-power-norm}
  \uses{def:l2norm, def:kron-power, lem:kron-power-inner}
  For every finite index set $I$, every vector $v:I\to\R$, and every natural
  $q$,
  \[
    \norm{v^{\otimes q}}=\norm{v}^{q}.
  \]
  The proof must use nonnegativity of Euclidean norms and the square identity
  from Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner}; it is not a purely ring-theoretic
  consequence.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:l2norm, def:kron-power, lem:kron-power-inner}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner} with $w=v$:
  \[
    \inner{v^{\otimes q}}{v^{\otimes q}}=\inner{v}{v}^{q}.
  \]
  By Definition~\ref{def:l2norm}, the left-hand side is
  $\norm{v^{\otimes q}}^{2}$ and $\inner{v}{v}=\norm{v}^{2}$. Hence
  \[
    \norm{v^{\otimes q}}^{2}=(\norm{v}^{2})^{q}=(\norm{v}^{q})^{2}.
  \]
  Both $\norm{v^{\otimes q}}$ and $\norm{v}^{q}$ are nonnegative, so equality of
  their squares implies equality of the norms.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Cosine similarity of Kronecker powers]
  \label{lem:kron-power-cosine}
  \uses{def:cosine, def:kron-power, lem:kron-power-inner, lem:kron-power-norm}
  For nonzero vectors $v,w\in\R^{\ell}$ and every natural $q$,
  \[
    \cossim{v^{\otimes q}}{w^{\otimes q}}
    =
    \left(\cossim{v}{w}\right)^{q}.
  \]
  This is the exact identity needed in Lemma~\ref{lem:msd-tensor-reduction}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:cosine, def:kron-power, lem:kron-power-inner, lem:kron-power-norm}
  Expand cosine similarity and apply Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-inner} to the
  numerator and Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-norm} to both denominator factors:
  \[
    \cossim{v^{\otimes q}}{w^{\otimes q}}
    =
    \frac{\inner{v}{w}^{q}}{\norm{v}^{q}\norm{w}^{q}}.
  \]
  Since $v$ and $w$ are nonzero, their norms are nonzero. Rearranging powers in
  the field gives
  \[
    \frac{\inner{v}{w}^{q}}{\norm{v}^{q}\norm{w}^{q}}
    =
    \left(\frac{\inner{v}{w}}{\norm{v}\norm{w}}\right)^q
    =
    \left(\cossim{v}{w}\right)^q.
  \]
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Continuity is closed under sums, products and composition]
  \label{lem:continuity-closure}
  \lean{Continuous.comp}
  \mathlibok
  This leaf packages standard continuity declarations such as
  `Continuous.add`, `Continuous.sub`, `Continuous.mul`, `Continuous.comp`,
  `continuous_const`, and continuity of coordinate projections. Finite sums,
  finite products and compositions of continuous functions between
  finite-dimensional real vector spaces are continuous, as are constant maps,
  coordinate projections and affine scalar maps. Recalled so the
  piecewise-linear MLP constructions below can be shown continuous.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Continuity of max and min with a continuous argument]
  \label{lem:continuous-real-max-min}
  \lean{Continuous.max, Continuous.min}
  \mathlibok
  If $h : X \to \R$ is continuous and $c\in\R$ is constant, then the maps
  $x\mapsto \max(c,h(x))$ and $x\mapsto \min(c,h(x))$ are continuous. In Lean
  these are not proved by treating `max c` or `min c` as independently
  continuous curried functions; apply
  `Continuous.max continuous_const hh` and
  `Continuous.min continuous_const hh` to the full lambda expression.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Continuity of the affine divided map]
  \label{lem:continuous-affine-divided}
  \uses{lem:continuity-closure}
  For real numbers $a,b$ with $b>a$, the map
  \[
    y\mapsto \frac{y-a}{b-a}
  \]
  is continuous as a map $\R\to\R$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:continuity-closure}
  Since $b>a$, the denominator $b-a$ is nonzero. Rewrite division by the
  constant $b-a$ as multiplication by the constant $(b-a)^{-1}$:
  \[
    \frac{y-a}{b-a}=(y-a)(b-a)^{-1}.
  \]
  The map $y\mapsto y-a$ is continuous by continuity of the identity map,
  constants and subtraction, and multiplication by the constant $(b-a)^{-1}$
  preserves continuity. Thus the displayed affine-divided map is continuous.

  A Lean proof should expose this as a separate continuous term, for example:
  first prove `hden : b - a \ne 0`; then prove
  `h_aff : Continuous (fun y : \R => (y - a) / (b - a))` by rewriting
  `div_eq_mul_inv` and using continuity of subtraction and multiplication by a
  constant. This proof should not be hidden inside a later `continuity` call.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Continuity of finite coordinate products]
  \label{lem:continuous-finite-product}
  \lean{continuous_finsetProd}
  \mathlibok
  Let $I$ be finite and let $h_i : X\to\R$ be continuous for every $i\in I$.
  Then $x\mapsto \prod_{i\in I} h_i(x)$ is continuous. In Lean, for a product
  over all coordinates $i:\mathrm{Fin}\,\ell$, use
  `continuous_finsetProd Finset.univ` and prove each factor continuous.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Continuity of the clipped affine threshold]
  \label{lem:continuous-clipped-affine}
  \uses{lem:continuous-affine-divided, lem:continuous-real-max-min}
  For real numbers $a,b$ with $b>a$, the function
  \[
    g(y)=\max\!\left(0,\min\!\left(1,\frac{y-a}{b-a}\right)\right)
  \]
  is continuous as a map $\R\to\R$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:continuous-affine-divided, lem:continuous-real-max-min}
  By Lemma~\ref{lem:continuous-affine-divided}, the inner affine-divided map
  \[
    h(y)=\frac{y-a}{b-a}
  \]
  is continuous. Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:continuous-real-max-min} to the continuous
  map $h$ and the constant $1$ to obtain continuity of
  \[
    y\mapsto \min(1,h(y)).
  \]
  Call this continuous map $h_{\min}$. Applying
  Lemma~\ref{lem:continuous-real-max-min} again, now to $h_{\min}$ and the
  constant $0$, gives continuity of
  \[
    y\mapsto \max(0,h_{\min}(y))
    =
    \max\!\left(0,\min\!\left(1,\frac{y-a}{b-a}\right)\right).
  \]

  For a Lean proof, do not use the tactic `continuity` for this node, because it
  may create unprovable curried goals such as `Continuous (max 0)` or
  `Continuous (min 1)`. The intended proof is the direct one:
  define
  `h_aff : Continuous (fun y : \R => (y - a) / (b - a))` using
  Lemma~\ref{lem:continuous-affine-divided}; then set
  `h_min : Continuous (fun y : \R => min 1 ((y - a) / (b - a))) :=
  Continuous.min continuous_const h_aff`; finally conclude with
