  Boolean is true exactly on OV yes instances. The runtime field is
  \[
    T_{\OV\leftarrow\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(n,\ell)
      \le C n\ell+
        C\sum_{r=0}^{\ell}\sum_{s=0}^{\ell}
          T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(|S_r|,|S_s|,\ell)
      \le C'(\ell+1)^2 T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(n,\ell)+C''n\ell,
  \]
  which preserves truly subquadratic time up to polynomial factors in $\ell$.
  The first inequality is the primary runtime accounting theorem, because each
  oracle call has its own color-class sizes. The witness must define
  \[
    \operatorname{weightCallRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}},V)
      =
      c_{\mathrm{partition}}n\ell
      +
      c_{\mathrm{calls}}
      \sum_{r=0}^{\ell}\sum_{s=0}^{\ell}
        T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(|S_r|,|S_s|,\ell)
      +
      c_{\mathrm{inspect}}(\ell+1)^2\ell
  \]
  and then prove the displayed bounds from this definition. A runtime formula
  using only $T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(n,n,\ell)$, or using
  $(\ell+1)^2T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(n,n,\ell)$ as the sole runtime without the
  double sum over $|S_r|,|S_s|$, is too coarse for this witness and is rejected.
  The coarser bound by $(\ell+1)^2T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(n,\ell)$ may appear only
  as a second theorem derived from monotonicity after the double-sum runtime
  has been stated.
  The weight-class correctness theorem must be the chain
  \[
  \begin{aligned}
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)
    &\Longleftrightarrow
      \exists r,s,\exists v\in S_r,\exists u\in S_s,\ \inner{v}{u}=0\\
    &\Longleftrightarrow
      \exists r,s,\ 
      \max_{v\in S_r,\ u\in S_s}\inner{v}{\overline u}=r\\
    &\Longleftrightarrow
      \exists r,s,\ 
      \operatorname{callScore}(V,r,s,o_{r,s})=r
      \quad\text{for every valid oracle answer }o_{r,s}.
  \end{aligned}
  \]
  The middle equivalence uses the fact that for $v\in S_r$,
  $\inner{v}{\overline u}\le r$ for every $u$, with equality iff
  $\inner{v}{u}=0$. A theorem that only restates
  ``there exists an orthogonal pair in some weight classes'' without the
  maximum-over-complements equality does not satisfy this node.

  In field form, the audited witness contains at least
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{weight}(v):& \norm{v}_1,\\
    \operatorname{weightClass}(V,r):& S_r=\{v_i:\norm{v_i}_1=r\},\\
    \operatorname{complementVector}(u):&
      \overline u\text{ with }\overline u[h]=1-u[h],\\
    \operatorname{callFamily}(V):&
      \{(S_r,\overline{S_s}) : 0\le r,s\le\ell\},\\
    \operatorname{callScore}(r,s,o):&
      \inner{v_o}{\overline u_o}\text{ for the returned cross pair }o,\\
    \operatorname{reconstruct}(V,\operatorname{answers}):&
      \mathrm{true}\Longleftrightarrow
      \exists r,s,\ \operatorname{callScore}(r,s,\operatorname{answers}_{r,s})=r,\\
    \operatorname{complementInner}:&
      v\in S_r,\ u\in S_s\Rightarrow
      \inner{v}{\overline u}=r-\inner{v}{u},\\
    \operatorname{weightClassCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)\Longleftrightarrow
      \exists r,s,\ \max_{v\in S_r,w\in\overline{S_s}}\inner{v}{w}=r,\\
    \operatorname{runtimeWeightCalls}:&
      \text{the displayed double-sum runtime bound.}
  \end{array}
  \]
  None of these fields may be replaced by a single
  $\operatorname{FGReduction}$ field, a $\TSQAlg$ implication, or an abstract
  algorithm-transfer theorem. The returned score must be compared to the
  concrete weight $r$ of the left class, not merely to an unspecified threshold.
  A witness that is only
  $\operatorname{Nonempty}(\operatorname{FGReduction})$ or only an opaque
  implication from bichromatic Max-IP algorithms to OV algorithms omits the
  construction required here.
  In particular, the projection named `thresholdEquivalence' must have the
  concrete type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{thresholdEquivalence}(V):\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists r,s,\ 
      \max_{v\in S_r,\ u\in S_s}\inner{v}{\overline u}=r,
  \end{array}
  \]
  or the equivalent three-line chain displayed above with the valid oracle
  scores. A field whose type is
  $\operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)\leftrightarrow\operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)$ is
  explicitly rejected even if it is named `thresholdEquivalence'. Similarly,
  `runtimeWeightCalls' must unfold to a statement about the named
  $\operatorname{weightCallRuntime}$ double sum over
  $T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(|S_r|,|S_s|,\ell)$. It is rejected if every oracle call
  in the runtime is charged as $T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(n,n,\ell)$ without first
  defining the concrete calls at sizes $|S_r|$ and $|S_s|$ and proving a
  separate monotonicity-based coarse bound.

  The audit should also reject the following weaker field shapes, even if the
  surrounding witness has the right name. A field
  \[
    \operatorname{thresholdEquivalence}(V):
      \operatorname{OVYes}(V)\Longleftrightarrow\operatorname{OVYes}(V)
  \]
  is not the threshold equivalence. A field
  `weightClassCorrect' which only says that every vector belongs to some
  weight class, or that an orthogonal pair can be assigned weights, is not the
  Max-IP reduction correctness theorem; it must contain the equality
  $\max_{v\in S_r,u\in S_s}\inner{v}{\overline u}=r$ and the iff to OV yes.
  Finally, the runtime projection must have the double-sum form
  \[
    \operatorname{weightCallRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}},V)
    =
    c_{\mathrm{partition}}n\ell+
    c_{\mathrm{calls}}\sum_{r=0}^{\ell}\sum_{s=0}^{\ell}
      T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(|S_r|,|S_s|,\ell)
    +c_{\mathrm{inspect}}(\ell+1)^2\ell.
  \]
  Charging every call as $T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(n,n,\ell)$ is permitted only in a
  separately named derived coarse bound after the concrete child-sized calls and
  the displayed runtime definition have already been exposed.

  Trial-8 alignment requirement: the correctness proof must not stop at
  assigning every vector to some weight class. The witness has a field
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{weightClassOrthogonalIff}(V):\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{OVYes}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists r,s,\exists v\in S_r,\exists u\in S_s,\
      \inner{v}{u}=0,
  \end{array}
  \]
  and a separate field
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{complementMaxIffZero}(V,r,s):\\
    \qquad
    \left(\exists v\in S_r,\exists u\in S_s,\inner{v}{u}=0\right)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \max_{v\in S_r,u\in S_s}\inner{v}{\overline u}=r .
  \end{array}
  \]
  The exported `thresholdEquivalence' must be the composition of these two
  fields:
  \[
    \operatorname{OVYes}(V)\Longleftrightarrow
    \exists r,s,\max_{v\in S_r,u\in S_s}\inner{v}{\overline u}=r .
  \]
  The reconstruction theorem then uses valid oracle answers
  $o_{r,s}$ for every concrete call and states
  \[
    \operatorname{reconstruct}(V,\operatorname{answers})=\mathrm{true}
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{OVYes}(V),
  \]
  where `reconstruct' unfolds to
  $\exists r,s,\operatorname{callScore}(V,r,s,o_{r,s})=r$. A field named
  `weightClassCorrect' that only proves each row has some weight, or a field
  named `thresholdEquivalence' whose type is
  `OVYes V ↔ OVYes V', is explicitly not the reduction correctness theorem.
  Likewise, the runtime package has separate projections
  `weightCallRuntimeDef',
  `weightCallRuntimeBoundByDoubleSum', and
  `weightCallRuntimeCoarseBound'. The first two must mention the double sum
  $\sum_r\sum_s T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(|S_r|,|S_s|,\ell)$; only the third may use
  a monotonicity-derived coarse charge by
  $(\ell+1)^2T_{\mathrm{BMaxIP}}(n,n,\ell)$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:maxip, def:bichromatic-maxip, def:ov, def:inner-prod}
  Given an $\OV_{n,\ell}$ instance $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in \{0,1\}^{\ell}$,
  partition the vectors into subsets $S_1, \ldots, S_{\ell}$ where $S_j$ contains
  all vectors with exactly $j$ ones. For each pair $1 \le i,j \le \ell$ let
  $\bar S_j$ consist of the vectors in $S_j$ with all entries flipped. Then for
  any $v \in S_i$ and $w \in \bar S_j$ (so $w = \bar u$ with $u \in S_j$), we have
  $\inner{v}{w} = i - \inner{v}{u}$, hence $\inner{v}{\bar u} = i$ iff
  $\inner{v}{u} = 0$. Therefore running the bichromatic Max-IP algorithm
  $\mathcal A$ on $(S_i, \bar S_j)$ and testing whether the maximum inner product
  equals $i$ reveals whether there is an orthogonal pair with one vector in $S_i$
  and one in $S_j$. Doing this for all $\ell^2$ pairs decides OV. The total time
  is $\bigO(\ell^{2}\cdot n^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell)) =
  \bigO(n^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell))$.
\end{proof}

\chapter{Hardness of document similarity}

\begin{theorem}[Hardness of $\gamma$-LSD, Theorem 3.1]
  \label{thm:gamma-lsd-hardness}
  \uses{def:gamma-lsd, def:ov, def:cosine, def:inner-prod, assumption:seth, conjecture:ovc, def:no-tsq-alg, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  Assuming SETH or OVC, for every $\eps>0$ there exists a constant $c>0$ such
  that $\NoTSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\LSD_{n,\ell}}$ for every $\gamma \ge 1$ when
  $\ell = \logDim(c,n)$.

  The declaration audited at this label must expose the reduction package
  $\operatorname{OVToGammaLSDHardnessWitness}$ used to derive the lower bound.
  This package is the theorem's main data. It is not a field named
  `lowerBound', not a proposition $\NoTSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\LSD}$ by itself,
  and not $\operatorname{Nonempty}(\operatorname{FGReduction})$ with hidden
  internals. A lower-bound proposition may be derived from the package only
  after the concrete maps, correctness proofs and runtime transfer below have
  been provided.
  Its source slice is the nonempty logarithmic regime
  $\ell=\logDim(c,n)$ for all sufficiently large $n$, and its target parameter
  is the same $(n,\ell,\gamma)$ with $\gamma\ge1$. For an OV instance
  $V=(v_1,\ldots,v_n)$ it defines
  \[
    \operatorname{hasZero}(V)
      \Longleftrightarrow \exists i,\ v_i=0^\ell,
    \qquad
    \operatorname{toLSD}(V)=
      \begin{cases}
        \text{unused} & \text{if }\operatorname{hasZero}(V),\\
        V & \text{otherwise,}
      \end{cases}
  \]
  so the $\gamma$-LSD oracle is called only on the valid nonzero-vector
  instance $V$ when no zero vector is present. Given an oracle output pair
  $(i^*,j^*)$, the reconstructed OV answer is
  \[
    \mathrm{true}
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{hasZero}(V)\ \vee\
    \inner{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}}=0 .
  \]
  The witness includes an explicit oracle-call field
  \[
    \operatorname{calls}(V)=
      \begin{cases}
        \varnothing & \text{if }\operatorname{hasZero}(V),\\
        \{\,V\,\} & \text{otherwise, viewed as a valid }
          \gamma\text{-}\LSD_{n,\ell}\text{ instance,}
      \end{cases}
  \]
  and an answer-reconstruction field
  \[
    \operatorname{reconstruct}(V,\operatorname{answers})
      =
      \begin{cases}
        \mathrm{true} & \text{if }\operatorname{hasZero}(V),\\
        \bigl(\inner{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}}=0\bigr)
          & \text{for the returned LSD pair }(i^*,j^*)\text{ otherwise.}
      \end{cases}
  \]
  Thus a zero-vector OV instance is answered before the LSD oracle is called,
  and a nonzero instance is sent unchanged to the concrete nonzero-binary input
  relation of Definition~\ref{def:gamma-lsd}.
  In the nonzero branch the witness must also expose the concrete oracle answer
  and its validity proof:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{lsdOracleAnswer}(V,\mathcal A)
      &: \operatorname{GammaLSDOut}(n,\ell,\gamma,V),\\
    \operatorname{lsdOracleCorrect}(V,\mathcal A)
      &: \operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}
         (n,\ell,\gamma,V,
          \operatorname{lsdOracleAnswer}(V,\mathcal A)),\\
    \operatorname{returnedPair}(V,\mathcal A)
      &:=(i^*,j^*)=
        \operatorname{lsdOracleAnswer}(V,\mathcal A).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The nonzero reconstruction equation is then
  \[
    \operatorname{reconstruct}(V,\operatorname{answers}_{\mathcal A})
    =
    \bigl(\inner{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}}=0\bigr),
  \]
  where $(i^*,j^*)$ is exactly the output of the gamma-LSD oracle on $V$. A
  correctness proof that reasons about an arbitrary pair, or about an erased
  answer with no $\operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}$ proof, does not transfer OV
  correctness.
  The package has explicit parameter-regime fields:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{sourceSlice}:&
      \ell=\logDim(c,n)\wedge n\ge n_0,\\
    \operatorname{sourceRegime\_iff}:&
      \operatorname{SrcRegime}(n,\ell)
      \Longleftrightarrow n\ge n_0\wedge \ell=\logDim(c,n),\\
    \operatorname{targetParam}:&
      (n,\ell,\gamma)\text{ for the concrete }
      \gamma\text{-}\LSD\text{ family},\\
    \operatorname{targetParam\_eq}:&
      \operatorname{targetParam}(n,\ell,\gamma)=(n,\logDim(c,n),\gamma)
      \text{ on }\operatorname{sourceSlice}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The variable $\gamma$ in these fields is universally quantified and is the
  same $\gamma$ appearing in the target family, the oracle call, the validity
  relation, the reconstructed algorithm, and the runtime. The witness is
  rejected if any of these fields are specialized to $\gamma=1$, if
  `targetParam' drops $\gamma$, or if the oracle-correctness theorem has the
  type for $\operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}(n,\ell,1,V,o)$ instead of
  $\operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}(n,\ell,\gamma,V,o)$ under the explicit
  hypothesis $\gamma\ge1$.
  The exported lower-bound theorem must be parameterized by this same source
  slice and target parameter. It is rejected if its conclusion is merely
  $\NoTSQAlg{\operatorname{def\_gamma\_lsd.family}}$ with no bound
  $(n,\ell,\gamma)$ parameter or no equation $\ell=\logDim(c,n)$.
  The package therefore contains a named lower-bound projection
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{lowerBoundOnLogSlice}:\\
    \qquad
    \forall \eps>0,\ \exists c>0,\ \forall n,\ell,\gamma,\ 
    n\ge n_0\to \ell=\logDim(c,n)\to \gamma\ge1\to\\
    \qquad\qquad
    \NoTSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\LSD_{n,\ell}} .
  \end{array}
  \]
  The conclusion must mention the instantiated parameter triple
  $(n,\ell,\gamma)$ of the concrete $\gamma$-LSD family. It is not enough to
  prove a lower bound for an uninstantiated family value or a proposition whose
  hypotheses do not include $\ell=\logDim(c,n)$.
  Zero-vector correctness is a concrete field, not an excluded case:
  \[
    \operatorname{zeroCaseCorrect}:
      \operatorname{hasZero}(V)\Longrightarrow
      \operatorname{reconstruct}(V,\varnothing)=\mathrm{true}
      \ \wedge\
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V).
  \]
  This field must be paired with the defining equation for the zero branch,
  \[
    \operatorname{reconstruct\_zero}(h):
      \operatorname{reconstruct}(V,\varnothing)=\mathrm{true}
      \quad\text{for }h:\operatorname{hasZero}(V),
  \]
  and with a proof
  \[
    \operatorname{hasZero\_to\_OVYes}(h):
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V).
  \]
  The proof of `hasZero_to_OVYes' must exhibit an index $i$ with
  $v_i=0^\ell$ and then a distinct partner index $j$ guaranteed by the source
  regime $n\ge2$, showing $\inner{v_i}{v_j}=0$. It is not enough to invoke
  classical excluded middle for $\operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)$.
  For the nonzero branch the witness must contain
  \[
    \operatorname{nonzeroBranchCorrect}:
      \neg\operatorname{hasZero}(V)\Longrightarrow
      \left(
        \operatorname{reconstruct}(V,\operatorname{answers})=\mathrm{true}
        \Longleftrightarrow
        \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)
      \right).
  \]
  A field with conclusion
  $\operatorname{hasZero}(V)\to
  (\operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)\vee\neg\operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V))$ is just
  excluded middle and is rejected; it does not prove that the constructed
  reduction answers true on the zero-vector branch.
  Likewise, a theorem named `zeroCaseCorrect' whose conclusion does not mention
  both `reconstruct' and `OVYes' is rejected, even if a separate lower-bound
  proposition is present.
  The package contains the zero-cosine equivalence
  \[
    v_i\ne0,\ v_j\ne0
    \Longrightarrow
    \bigl(\cossim{v_i}{v_j}=0
      \Longleftrightarrow \inner{v_i}{v_j}=0\bigr),
  \]
  the minimum-zero equivalence
  \[
    \min_{p\ne q}\cossim{v_p}{v_q}=0
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)
  \]
  under $\neg\operatorname{hasZero}(V)$, and the approximation-zero field
  \[
    \operatorname{ValidOut}_{\gamma\text{-}\LSD}(V,(i^*,j^*))
    \wedge \gamma\ge1
    \Longrightarrow
    \left(
      \min_{p\ne q}\cossim{v_p}{v_q}=0
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \cossim{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}}=0
    \right).
  \]
  The last field must unfold the $\gamma$-LSD validity relation:
  if
  \[
    m=\min_{p\ne q}\cossim{v_p}{v_q}
    \quad\text{and}\quad
    m\le c^*\le\gamma m,\qquad c^*=\cossim{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}},
  \]
  then, using $m\ge0$ for nonzero binary vectors and $\gamma\ge1$,
  \[
    m=0 \Longleftrightarrow c^*=0.
  \]
  This is the multiplicative-zero argument; it cannot be replaced by a generic
  approximation theorem or by an abstract reduction correctness field.
  The nonzero branch correctness field is explicitly derived from these data:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{oracleOutputZeroCorrect}(V,\mathcal A):\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}
      (n,\ell,\gamma,V,(i^*,j^*))
    \to \gamma\ge1\to \neg\operatorname{hasZero}(V)\to\\
    \qquad
    \left(
      \inner{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}}=0
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)
    \right).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Its proof must use, in order, the gamma-LSD validity inequalities for the
  returned oracle pair, nonnegativity of binary cosine values, the
  minimum-zero equivalence, and the zero-cosine/zero-inner-product equivalence.
  A field named $\operatorname{nonzeroBranchCorrect}$ that does not take the
  oracle validity proof as an input, or that does not mention
  $\operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}$, is not this correctness theorem.
  Its runtime field is
  \[
    T_{\OV\leftarrow\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell)
      \le C\bigl(n\ell+T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)\bigr),
  \]
  and it proves this bound preserves the same positive truly-subquadratic
  exponent on the logarithmic dimension slice. The runtime field's left side is
  the runtime of the constructed OV algorithm with the zero-vector scan, at most
  one LSD oracle call, and the final inner-product test. It is not the
  tautology $n\ell+T_{\gamma\LSD}\le n\ell+T_{\gamma\LSD}$ and it is not a
  stand-alone asymptotic lower-bound proposition. A declaration that states only
  the high-level lower-bound proposition, without these maps, equivalences,
  reconstructed answer and runtime accounting, is not this theorem.
  As with Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-harder-ov}, this runtime appears through a named
  definition and a separate bound:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{gammaLSDReductionRuntime}(T_{\gamma\LSD},n,\ell,\gamma)
      &: \R_{\ge0},\\
    \operatorname{gammaLSDRuntimeDef}:&
      \operatorname{gammaLSDReductionRuntime}(T_{\gamma\LSD},n,\ell,\gamma)
      =
      c_{\mathrm{zeroScan}}n\ell+
      c_{\mathrm{call}}T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)+
      c_{\mathrm{test}}\ell+
      c_{\mathrm{branch}},\\
    \operatorname{gammaLSDRuntimeBound}:&
      \operatorname{gammaLSDReductionRuntime}(T_{\gamma\LSD},n,\ell,\gamma)
      \le C\bigl(n\ell+T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)\bigr).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The bound is rejected if the left-hand side is the expression
  $n\ell+T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)$ rather than the named constructed
  runtime, or if the runtime definition omits either the zero-vector scan or the
  target gamma-LSD oracle call.
  The projection named `runtimeTransfer' must be a package or theorem about
  this named runtime, not the final inequality alone. Its statement must expose
  both
  $\operatorname{gammaLSDReductionRuntime}$ and
  $\operatorname{gammaLSDRuntimeDef}$, and its bound conclusion must have
  $\operatorname{gammaLSDReductionRuntime}
  (T_{\gamma\LSD},n,\ell,\gamma)$ as the left-hand side. A proof term whose
  only runtime content is
  $T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)+n\ell
  \le C(T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)+n\ell)$ is a tautology about the oracle
  runtime, not a constructed OV runtime, and is rejected. The projection named
  `lowerBoundStatement' is also accepted only as a derived theorem whose proof
  invokes the concrete `runtimeTransfer', `oracleOutputZeroCorrect',
  `zeroCaseCorrect', and the source-regime fields above. A standalone
  lower-bound proposition attached to the witness, with no definitional path to
  the constructed OV algorithm and its runtime, does not satisfy this theorem.

  Concretely, the runtime transfer package contains all of the following
  projections:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{constructedOVRun}:&
      \text{scan for a zero vector; otherwise call the }
      \gamma\text{-LSD oracle and test the returned inner product},\\
    \operatorname{constructedOVCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{constructedOVRun}(V)=\mathrm{true}
      \Longleftrightarrow \operatorname{OVYes}(V),\\
    \operatorname{constructedOVRuntime}:&
      \operatorname{constructedOVRuntime}(T_{\gamma\LSD},n,\ell,\gamma)
      =
      \operatorname{gammaLSDReductionRuntime}
        (T_{\gamma\LSD},n,\ell,\gamma),\\
    \operatorname{runtimeTransfer}:&
      \operatorname{gammaLSDReductionRuntime}
        (T_{\gamma\LSD},n,\ell,\gamma)
      \le C(n\ell+T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Each projection must retain the arbitrary $\gamma\ge1$. A proof of the
  theorem for the single case $\gamma=1$ proves only exact LSD hardness and is
  not this node.

  Trial-8 alignment requirement: `runtimeTransfer' is a record whose first
  field is the constructed algorithm, not a bound on a free expression. It must
  expose
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{ovFromGammaLSDRun}(V):&
      \text{if }\operatorname{hasZero}(V)\text{ then true, otherwise }
      \inner{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}}=0
      \text{ for the oracle pair }(i^*,j^*),\\
    \operatorname{ovFromGammaLSDRun\_zero}:&
      \operatorname{hasZero}(V)\to
      \operatorname{ovFromGammaLSDRun}(V)=\mathrm{true},\\
    \operatorname{ovFromGammaLSDRun\_nonzero}:&
      \neg\operatorname{hasZero}(V)\to
      \operatorname{ovFromGammaLSDRun}(V)=
      \left(\inner{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}}=0\right),\\
    \operatorname{ovFromGammaLSDCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{ovFromGammaLSDRun}(V)=\mathrm{true}
      \Longleftrightarrow \operatorname{OVYes}(V),\\
    \operatorname{ovFromGammaLSDRuntimeDef}:&
      T_{\mathrm{constructed}}(n,\ell,\gamma)
      =
      c_{\mathrm{zeroScan}}n\ell+
      c_{\mathrm{call}}T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)+
      c_{\mathrm{test}}\ell+c_{\mathrm{branch}},\\
    \operatorname{ovFromGammaLSDRuntimeBound}:&
      T_{\mathrm{constructed}}(n,\ell,\gamma)
      \le C(n\ell+T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The field `lowerBoundStatement' is a theorem derived from this record plus
  OVC/SETH; it is not an independent field that may be postulated without a run,
  correctness proof and constructed runtime. The term
  $T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)+n\ell\le
  C(T_{\gamma\LSD}(n,\ell,\gamma)+n\ell)$ may appear only as an intermediate
  inequality after rewriting `ovFromGammaLSDRuntimeDef'; it is not the type of
  `runtimeTransfer'. The nonzero correctness theorem must use the actual oracle
  output and the proof
  $\operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}(n,\ell,\gamma,V,(i^*,j^*))$; pairwise
  zero-cosine facts without this validity proof do not prove the reduction.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:gamma-lsd, def:ov, def:cosine, def:inner-prod, conjecture:ovc, thm:seth-implies-ovc, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  Assume for contradiction that some algorithm $\mathcal A$ solves
  $\gamma\text{-}\LSD_{n, \logDim(c,n)}$ in time $\bigO(n^{2-\eps})$ for some
  $\gamma \ge 1$, $\eps>0$ and \emph{every} constant $c>0$. We show that
  $\OV_{n, \logDim(c,n)}$ can then be solved in $\bigO(n^{2-\eps})$ time for
  every $c$, refuting OVC (and hence SETH, by
  Theorem~\ref{thm:seth-implies-ovc}).

  Given $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in \{0,1\}^{\ell}$ with
  $\ell = \logDim(c,n)$: if any vector is the zero vector (checkable in
  $\bigO(n\ell)$ time) output "yes". Otherwise run $\mathcal A$ to obtain
  $i^{*}, j^{*}$ with
  \[
    \min_{1 \le i,j \le n} \cossim{v_i}{v_j}
    \le \cossim{v_{i^{*}}}{v_{j^{*}}}
    \le \gamma \cdot \min_{1 \le i,j \le n} \cossim{v_i}{v_j}.
  \]
  Since all $\norm{v_i} > 0$, the quantity $\min_{i,j}\cossim{v_i}{v_j}$ equals
  $0$ iff there is an orthogonal pair (cosine similarity $0 \Leftrightarrow$
  inner product $0$). As $\gamma \ge 1$, $\cossim{v_{i^{*}}}{v_{j^{*}}} = 0$ iff
  the true minimum is $0$, i.e.\ iff $\mathcal A$ returns an orthogonal pair.
  Thus checking whether $\inner{v_{i^{*}}}{v_{j^{*}}} = 0$ decides
  $\OV_{n,\ell}$. The total time is $\bigO(n\ell + n^{2-\eps}) =
  \bigO(n^{2-\eps})$, refuting SETH/OVC.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Exact LSD transfers to $1$-LSD]
  \label{lem:lsd-exact-to-gamma-one-transfer}
  \uses{def:lsd, def:gamma-lsd, def:tsq-alg-exists}
  An exact $\LSD_{n,\ell}$ search algorithm yields a
  $1\text{-}\LSD_{n,\ell}$ approximation algorithm by returning the same pair.
  The transfer witness has projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{exactSearchRun}(V)&=\operatorname{run}_{\LSD}(V),\\
    \operatorname{exactSearchCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{LSDValidOut}(V,\operatorname{exactSearchRun}(V))
      \to
      \operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}
        (n,\ell,1,V,\operatorname{exactSearchRun}(V)),\\
    \operatorname{exactSearchRuntimeDef}:&
      T_{\mathrm{exact}\to\gamma=1}(n,\ell)
      =T_{\LSD}(n,\ell)+c_{\mathrm{return}}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  This node owns only the exact-search-to-$\gamma=1$ transfer.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:lsd, def:gamma-lsd}
  If $o$ is an exact minimizer, then its cosine score equals
  $\operatorname{LSDOpt}(V)$.  Unfolding the $\gamma$-LSD validity relation with
  $\gamma=1$ gives the two inequalities
  $\operatorname{LSDOpt}(V)\le s(o)\le\operatorname{LSDOpt}(V)$.  The runtime is
  the exact oracle call plus the constant cost of returning the same pair.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[LSD hardness transfers to larger dimensions]
  \label{lem:lsd-larger-dimension-transfer}
  \uses{def:lsd, def:cosine, def:no-tsq-alg, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  For $\ell'\ge\ell$, padding a nonzero binary vector by zeros,
  \[
    \operatorname{pad}_{\ell,\ell'}(v)=(v,0^{\ell'-\ell}),
  \]
  preserves nonzeroness and all pairwise cosine similarities.  Therefore a
  solver in dimension $\ell'$ gives a solver in dimension $\ell$, with runtime
  \[
    T_{\mathrm{pad}}(n,\ell,\ell')
      =
      c_{\mathrm{pad}}n\ell'
      +T_{\LSD,\ell'}(n)
      +c_{\mathrm{unpad}}.
  \]
  This node owns the padding map, the inner-product/norm/cosine preservation
  equations, output unpadding, correctness, and runtime transfer used in
  Corollary~\ref{cor:lsd-hardness}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:lsd, def:cosine}
  Padding by trailing zeros does not change an inner product and does not
  change a Euclidean norm.  Since all vectors remain nonzero, cosine similarity
  is preserved.  An oracle output pair for the padded instance is already a
  pair of original indices, so unpadding returns the same pair.  The runtime is
  the padding cost, one target oracle call, and constant unpadding overhead.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Bichromatic $\gamma$-LSD transfers to monochromatic $\gamma$-LSD]
  \label{lem:lsd-bichromatic-transfer}
  \uses{def:gamma-lsd, def:bichromatic-gamma-lsd, def:tsq-alg-exists, lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}
  A bichromatic $\gamma$-LSD solver yields a monochromatic $\gamma$-LSD solver
  by the recursive split-tree construction over one list.  At an internal node
  $U=U_L\cup U_R$ the concrete oracle call is
  \[
    \operatorname{cosineCrossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R),
  \]
  and the node optimum decomposes as
  \[
    m_U=\min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U))),
  \]
  where the three terms are the cross-color, left-recursive, and
  right-recursive cosine minima.  The reconstructed candidate is the smallest
  cosine-score candidate among the valid cross answer and the two recursive
  answers, and it satisfies the $\gamma$-approximation inequalities for $m_U$.
  This node owns only the cosine split-tree transfer and its runtime sum.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:gamma-lsd, def:bichromatic-gamma-lsd, lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}
  The split tree and runtime accounting are the same as
  Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}; replace each inner-product score
  by cosine similarity and each bichromatic Min-IP call by the concrete
  bichromatic $\gamma$-LSD call $(U_L,U_R)$.  Every original distinct pair is
  represented either in the cross call or in one child recursion, giving the
  displayed minimum decomposition.  Selecting the smallest among valid
  $\gamma$-approximate branch candidates preserves the same approximation
  factor for the parent.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Some LSD threshold family is hard]
  \label{lem:lsd-hard-threshold-transfer}
  \uses{def:lsd, def:lsd-dec, def:no-tsq-alg, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  If exact $\LSD_{n,\ell}$ is hard on the logarithmic slice, then there exists
  a threshold $t\in[0,1]$ such that the concrete decision family
  $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$ is hard on the same slice:
  \[
    \exists t:\R,\quad 0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \NoTSQAlg{\LSD_{n,\ell,t}}.
  \]
  The transfer uses the finite spectrum
  \[
    \mathcal T_{\ell}
    =
    \left\{\frac{s}{\sqrt{ab}}:
      0\le s\le\ell,\ 1\le a,b\le\ell\right\}
  \]
  of possible cosine values of nonzero binary vectors.  This node owns the
  threshold set, membership of all binary cosine values in it, the exact-search
  reconstruction from threshold oracle answers, and the existential hard
  threshold conclusion with the witness $t$ bound in the family argument.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:lsd, def:lsd-dec}
  For nonzero binary vectors, the numerator of cosine similarity is an integer
  $s$ with $0\le s\le\ell$, while the squared norms are positive integers
  $a,b\in\{1,\ldots,\ell\}$.  Hence every possible cosine value lies in
  $\mathcal T_\ell$.  If every threshold family
  $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$ for $t\in\mathcal T_\ell$ had a truly subquadratic solver,
  enumerating $\mathcal T_\ell$ and taking the least feasible threshold would
  recover an exact least-similarity pair in truly subquadratic time, contrary
  to exact LSD hardness.  Therefore at least one threshold family is hard.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Hardness of LSD and its variants, Corollary 3.2]
  \label{cor:lsd-hardness}
  \uses{def:lsd, def:gamma-lsd, def:bichromatic-gamma-lsd, def:lsd-dec, conjecture:ovc, assumption:seth, def:no-tsq-alg, def:log-parameter-regimes, thm:gamma-lsd-hardness, lem:lsd-exact-to-gamma-one-transfer, lem:lsd-larger-dimension-transfer, lem:lsd-bichromatic-transfer, lem:lsd-hard-threshold-transfer}
  Assuming SETH or OVC, for every $\eps>0$ there exists a constant $c>0$ such
  that $\NoTSQAlg{\LSD_{n,\ell}}$ when $\ell \ge \logDim(c,n)$. Moreover, the
  same lower bound holds for bichromatic
  $\gamma\text{-}\LSD_{n,\ell}$ for all $\gamma \ge 1$, and for $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$
  for some $t \in [0,1]$.

  The declaration audited at this label must be the corollary witness package
  $\operatorname{LSDHardnessCorollaryWitness}$ with four non-vacuous fields:
  \begin{itemize}
    \item \emph{exact-search transfer}: an algorithm for exact $\LSD_{n,\ell}$
      yields a $\gamma$-LSD algorithm with $\gamma=1$ by running the exact
      search algorithm and returning the same pair, with the proof that exact
      minimizers satisfy the $\gamma=1$ approximation relation;
    \item \emph{larger-dimension transfer}: for every $\ell'\ge\logDim(c,n)$,
      the embedding $v\mapsto(v,0,\ldots,0)\in\{0,1\}^{\ell'}$ preserves
      nonzeroness and all pairwise cosine similarities, so a solver in dimension
      $\ell'$ gives one on the logarithmic hard slice;
    \item \emph{bichromatic transfer}: a solver for bichromatic
      $\gamma$-LSD on two color classes yields a monochromatic $\gamma$-LSD
      solver by the standard recursive split construction over a single list,
      with the same split-tree, reconstruction and runtime accounting as
      Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}, but using cross-color cosine
      minima instead of inner-product minima;
    \item \emph{threshold transfer}: if every threshold family
      $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$ for $t\in[0,1]$ had a truly subquadratic algorithm, then
      exact $\LSD_{n,\ell}$ would be solved by enumerating or binary searching
      the finite set
      \[
        \mathcal T_{\ell}
        =
        \left\{\frac{s}{\sqrt{ab}}:
          0\le s\le\ell,\ 1\le a,b\le\ell\right\}
      \]
      of all possible cosine values of nonzero binary vectors and returning a
      pair at the least feasible threshold. The package must therefore prove the
      existential conclusion
      \[
        \exists t\in[0,1],\quad
        \NoTSQAlg{\LSD_{n,\ell,t}}
      \]
      on the logarithmic slice; it must not state a lower bound for an
      unspecified or all-purpose `def_lsd_dec' family without binding the
      witness threshold $t$.
  \end{itemize}
  The witness package itself must contain the concrete algorithms and maps
  listed below. A record with fields only of the form
  `TSQAlg A -> TSQAlg B' or
  `NoTSQAlg A -> NoTSQAlg B' is not this corollary; such implications may be
  exported as derived theorems only after the maps, output reconstruction and
  runtime fields below have been supplied.
  The four fields have the following required concrete shapes:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{exactToGammaOne}:&
      \operatorname{ValidOut}_{\LSD}(V,(i,j))
      \Rightarrow
      \operatorname{ValidOut}_{1\text{-}\LSD}(V,(i,j)),\\
    \operatorname{padToLargerDim}:&
      v\mapsto(v,0^{\ell'-\ell})\text{ with }
      \cossim{(v,0)}{(w,0)}=\cossim{v}{w},\\
    \operatorname{largerDimRuntime}:&
      T_{\LSD,\ell}(n)\le C(n\ell'+T_{\LSD,\ell'}(n)),\\
    \operatorname{bichromaticSplitTree}:&
      \text{the recursive halving tree over one list }V,\\
    \operatorname{bichromaticCosineNodeCorrectness}:&
      \min_{p\ne q\in U}\cossim{p}{q}
      =
      \min\!\left(
        \min_{p\in U_L,q\in U_R}\cossim{p}{q},
        \min_{p\ne q\in U_L}\cossim{p}{q},
        \min_{p\ne q\in U_R}\cossim{p}{q}
      \right),\\
    \operatorname{bichromaticGammaCorrectness}:&
      \text{best reconstructed cross/recursive candidate is a }
      \gamma\text{-approximate cosine minimum},\\
    \operatorname{thresholdValues}:&
      \mathcal T_\ell=
      \{s/\sqrt{ab}:0\le s\le\ell,\ 1\le a,b\le\ell\},\\
    \operatorname{thresholdSearchCorrectness}:&
      \text{enumerating }\mathcal T_\ell\text{ recovers the least cosine
      value and a minimizing pair},\\
    \operatorname{existsHardThreshold}:&
      \exists t,\ 0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \NoTSQAlg{\LSD_{n,\ell,t}}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  More explicitly, `exactToGammaOne' is a witness constructor, not a bare
  implication. Given an exact LSD oracle output $o=(i,j)$, it returns the same
  pair and proves
  \[
    \operatorname{LSDScore}(V,o)=\operatorname{LSDOpt}(V)
    \Longrightarrow
    \operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}(n,\ell,1,V,o)
  \]
  by unfolding the $\gamma$-LSD inequalities with $\gamma=1$. Its runtime field
  is
  \[
    T_{1\text{-}\LSD}(n,\ell)
      =
      T_{\LSD}(n,\ell)+c_{\mathrm{return}}
      \le C(T_{\LSD}(n,\ell)+1),
  \]
  so the constructed algorithm's runtime is tied to the exact oracle runtime.
  Therefore an `exact-search transfer' field whose type is only
  `TSQAlg LSD -> TSQAlg GammaLSD' is rejected unless the same field, after
  unfolding, exposes this returned pair, validity proof and runtime equation.
  In particular, the witness contains
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{exactToGammaOneRun}(V) &:=
      \operatorname{run}_{\LSD}(V),\\
    \operatorname{exactToGammaOneCorrect}(V) &:\
      \operatorname{LSDValidOut}(V,
        \operatorname{exactToGammaOneRun}(V))
      \to
      \operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}(n,\ell,1,V,
        \operatorname{exactToGammaOneRun}(V)),\\
    \operatorname{exactToGammaOneRuntimeDef}:&
      T_{1\text{-}\LSD}(n,\ell)
      =
      T_{\LSD}(n,\ell)+c_{\mathrm{return}}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  These are data of the transfer, not consequences hidden behind a
  $\operatorname{Nonempty}$ implication.

  The padding transfer must define, for every $\ell'\ge\ell$,
  \[
    \operatorname{pad}_{\ell,\ell'}(v)
      =(v,0^{\ell'-\ell})
  \]
  together with the three equations
  \[
    \inner{\operatorname{pad}(v)}{\operatorname{pad}(w)}
      =\inner{v}{w},\qquad
    \norm{\operatorname{pad}(v)}=\norm{v},\qquad
    \cossim{\operatorname{pad}(v)}{\operatorname{pad}(w)}
      =\cossim{v}{w}.
  \]
  It then maps an oracle output pair for the padded instance back to the same
  pair of original indices. A padding field that mentions only monotonicity of
  dimension, or only stores an abstract map without these three equations, does
  not prove the larger-dimension claim.
  The larger-dimension lower-bound conclusion must retain the concrete target
  parameter $\ell'$ and the hypothesis $\ell'\ge\logDim(c,n)$. It is rejected
  if it states a lower bound for an unparameterized family `def_lsd.family' or
  if the padding map is not projected from the witness.
  The field named $\operatorname{largerDimensionTransfer}$ must not have type
  $\mathrm{True}$. It is a package with projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{padInst}_{\ell,\ell'}(V)
      &: \LSDInst(n,\ell'),\\
    \operatorname{padInst\_row}:&
      \operatorname{padInst}_{\ell,\ell'}(V)_i
      =(v_i,0^{\ell'-\ell}),\\
    \operatorname{padCosine}:&
      \cossim{\operatorname{pad}(v_i)}{\operatorname{pad}(v_j)}
      =\cossim{v_i}{v_j},\\
    \operatorname{unpadOutput}:&
      \operatorname{LSDOut}(n,\ell',
        \operatorname{padInst}_{\ell,\ell'}(V))
      \to \operatorname{LSDOut}(n,\ell,V),\\
    \operatorname{largerDimensionCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{LSDValidOut}(n,\ell',
        \operatorname{padInst}_{\ell,\ell'}(V),o')
      \to
      \operatorname{LSDValidOut}(n,\ell,V,
        \operatorname{unpadOutput}(o')),\\
    \operatorname{largerDimensionRuntimeDef}:&
      T_{\mathrm{pad}}(n,\ell,\ell')
      =
      c_{\mathrm{pad}}n\ell'
      +T_{\LSD,\ell'}(n)
      +c_{\mathrm{unpad}}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The lower-bound transfer is derived from these projections. A generated field
  whose conclusion is only $\mathrm{True}$, or only says that larger dimension
  is harder without defining $\operatorname{padInst}_{\ell,\ell'}$, is rejected.

  The bichromatic transfer field is a cosine version of the recursive split
  witness. At every node $U=U_L\cup U_R$ it constructs the concrete
  bichromatic $\gamma$-LSD instance $(U_L,U_R)$, receives a valid cross-color
  output, recursively receives valid candidates from $U_L$ and $U_R$, and
  returns the candidate with smallest cosine score among the three. Its
  correctness theorem must use the decomposition
  \[
    m_U=\min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U)))
  \]
  where
  $m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)=\min_{p\in U_L,q\in U_R}\cossim{p}{q}$,
  $m_L(U)=\min_{p\ne q\in U_L}\cossim{p}{q}$, and
  $m_R(U)=\min_{p\ne q\in U_R}\cossim{p}{q}$. It is rejected if it only states
  an implication
  $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }\gamma\text{-}\LSD}\to
    \TSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\LSD}$, or if its node correctness repeats
  $\operatorname{LSDOpt}(U)$ on all three branches.
  Its call field must be the singleton concrete bichromatic instance
  \[
    \operatorname{cosineCallsAtNode}(U)
      =
      \{\,(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\gamma,(U_L,U_R))\,\},
  \]
  and its reconstruction must choose the smallest cosine-score candidate among
  the cross, left and right answers. These are not optional helper definitions.
  The field named $\operatorname{bichromaticTransfer}$ is not merely
  $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }\gamma\text{-}\LSD}\to
  \TSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\LSD}$. It must expose the split-tree projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{cosineCrossInst}(U)&=(U_L,U_R),\\
    \operatorname{cosineCallsAtNode\_eq}:&
      \operatorname{cosineCallsAtNode}(U)
      =
      \{\,(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\gamma,
          \operatorname{cosineCrossInst}(U))\,\},\\
    \operatorname{cosineCandidateSet}(U)&=
      \{o_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),o_L(U),o_R(U)\},\\
    \operatorname{cosineReconstructGamma}(U,\operatorname{answers})
      &\in
      \arg\min_{o\in\operatorname{cosineCandidateSet}(U)}
        \cossim{\operatorname{left}(o)}{\operatorname{right}(o)}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  Its correctness field is the displayed minimum decomposition for
  $m_U,m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),m_L(U),m_R(U)$ followed by the
  $\gamma$-approximation inequalities for the reconstructed candidate. A
  $\operatorname{Nonempty}$ implication, or a split field whose node
  correctness is $\mathrm{True}$, does not satisfy this transfer.

  The threshold transfer must bind a specific threshold family. It defines the
  finite set $\mathcal T_\ell$ above, proves that for every nonzero binary
  pair $(v,w)$ the value $\cossim{v}{w}$ belongs to $\mathcal T_\ell$, and
  defines
  \[
    t_{\min}(V)=\min\{t\in\mathcal T_\ell:
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\LSD_{n,\ell,t}}(V)\}.
  \]
  From threshold oracle answers on these finitely many $t$ values it recovers a
  pair attaining $t_{\min}(V)=\operatorname{LSDOpt}(V)$. The hard-threshold
  conclusion is therefore the dependent statement
  \[
    \operatorname{existsHardThreshold}:
    \exists t:\R,\ 0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \NoTSQAlg{(\operatorname{LSDThresholdFamily})(n,\ell,t)}.
  \]
  The family in this last display must be the concrete decision family from
  Definition~\ref{def:lsd-dec} instantiated at the returned threshold $t$. A
  conclusion about an uninstantiated `def_lsd_dec' object, or about a threshold
  chosen outside the witness package, is not this field.
  In particular, the statement
  \[
    \exists t,\ 0\le t\le1\wedge
      \NoTSQAlg{\operatorname{def\_lsd\_dec.family}}
  \]
  is explicitly rejected: the right-hand side does not apply the family to the
  witness parameter $(n,\ell,t)$ and therefore does not identify which
  threshold decision problem is hard.
  None of these fields may have type `True', `Unit', `True -> True', or be only
  an implication between abstract $\operatorname{TSQAlgorithm}$ existence
  propositions. In particular, the threshold field must quantify and return a
  threshold-specific family $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$ with the witness $t$ and proof
  $0\le t\le1$; the conclusion
  $\NoTSQAlg{\text{def\_lsd\_dec}}$ without a bound threshold is not this
  corollary.
  The threshold witness also exposes the instantiated family equation
  \[
    \operatorname{thresholdFamilyAt}(n,\ell,t)
      =
      \operatorname{LSDThresholdFamily}(n,\ell,t)
  \]
  and the hard-threshold field has exactly the dependent type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{existsHardThreshold}:\\
    \qquad
    \exists t:\R,\ 0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \NoTSQAlg{\operatorname{thresholdFamilyAt}(n,\ell,t)}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The variable $t$ returned by the existential must occur in the family
  argument on the right-hand side. The field is rejected if the right-hand side
  is independent of $t$, if it names only $\operatorname{def\_lsd\_dec}$ or
  $\operatorname{def\_lsd\_dec.family}$, or if the threshold range proof
  $0\le t\le1$ is not paired with the same $t$.
  These fields must retain the parameter regime
  $\ell\ge\logDim(c,n)$ and the bichromatic $\gamma$-LSD claim. A corollary
  statement that only mentions the abstract families
  $\LSD$, $\gamma$-LSD and $\LSD$-decision, or omits the existential threshold,
  is weaker than the paper's Corollary 3.2.
  The three transfer fields named by the critic are reserved names with
  non-vacuous meanings:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{largerDimensionTransfer}:&
      \text{the package containing } \operatorname{padInst},
      \operatorname{padInst\_row},\operatorname{padCosine},
      \operatorname{unpadOutput},\operatorname{largerDimensionCorrect},
      \operatorname{largerDimensionRuntimeDef};\\
    \operatorname{bichromaticTransfer}:&
      \text{the cosine split-tree package containing }
      \operatorname{cosineCrossInst},
      \operatorname{cosineCallsAtNode\_eq},
      \operatorname{cosineReconstructGamma},
      \operatorname{bichromaticCosineNodeCorrectness},
      \operatorname{bichromaticGammaCorrectness};\\
    \operatorname{thresholdTransfer}:&
      \text{the finite-spectrum package containing }
      \operatorname{thresholdValues},
      \operatorname{thresholdFamilyAt},
      \operatorname{thresholdSearchCorrectness},
      \operatorname{existsHardThreshold}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  None of these three fields may have type $\mathrm{True}$, $\mathrm{Unit}$, or
  only an implication between $\TSQAlg$ or $\NoTSQAlg$ propositions. If
  `largerDimensionTransfer' unfolds to `True', if `bichromaticTransfer' unfolds
  only to
  $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }\gamma\text{-}\LSD}\to
  \TSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\LSD}$, or if `thresholdTransfer' unfolds only to an
  abstract implication from all threshold solvers to exact LSD, the declaration
  is rejected. Each field must project the concrete maps, equations, returned
  candidates and runtime definitions listed in this node, and the derived
  lower-bound statements must be proved from those projections.

  The following field names have reserved concrete types in this corollary.
  `largerDimensionTransfer' is a record with the fields
  `padInst', `padInst_row', `padInner', `padNorm', `padCosine',
  `unpadOutput', `largerDimensionCorrect',
  `largerDimensionRuntime', `largerDimensionRuntimeDef', and
  `largerDimensionRuntimeBound'. It is rejected if it is a proposition, `True',
  or a bare lower-bound implication.
  `bichromaticTransfer' is a record with the fields
  `cosineSplitTree', `cosineCrossInst', `cosineCallsAtNode_eq',
  `cosineCandidateSet', `cosineReconstructGamma',
  `bichromaticCosineNodeCorrectness',
  `bichromaticGammaCorrectness', `cosineSplitRuntime',
  `cosineSplitRuntimeDef', and `cosineSplitRuntimeBound'. It is rejected if it
  is only
  $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }\gamma\text{-}\LSD}\to
    \TSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\LSD}$.
  `thresholdTransfer' is a record with the fields
  `thresholdValues', `cosineValue_mem_thresholdValues',
  `thresholdFamilyAt', `thresholdFamilyAt_eq',
  `thresholdSearchRun', `thresholdSearchCorrectness',
  `thresholdSearchRuntimeDef', and `existsHardThreshold'. The field
  `existsHardThreshold' must have the dependent type
  \[
    \exists t:\R,\ 0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \NoTSQAlg{\operatorname{thresholdFamilyAt}(n,\ell,t)},
  \]
  where the same existentially bound $t$ occurs in the family argument.
  Therefore a conclusion involving only `def_lsd_dec.family', or any family
  expression independent of $t$, does not satisfy the threshold part of the
  corollary.

  Trial-8 alignment requirement: the three transfer fields named in the audit
  are records with fixed projections, never propositions.
  `exactSearchTransfer' has projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{exactSearchRun}(V)&=\operatorname{run}_{\LSD}(V),\\
    \operatorname{exactSearchCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{LSDValidOut}(V,\operatorname{exactSearchRun}(V))
      \to
      \operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}
        (n,\ell,1,V,\operatorname{exactSearchRun}(V)),\\
    \operatorname{exactSearchRuntimeDef}:&
      T_{\mathrm{exact}\to\gamma=1}(n,\ell)
      =T_{\LSD}(n,\ell)+c_{\mathrm{return}}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  `largerDimensionTransfer' has type a record containing at least the padding
  instance, the row equation, `padInner', `padNorm', `padCosine',
  `unpadOutput', `largerDimensionCorrect',
  `largerDimensionRuntimeDef', and `largerDimensionRuntimeBound'. Its type is
  rejected if it is `True', `Unit', or a theorem with no `padInst' projection.
  `bichromaticTransfer' has type a cosine split-tree record whose correctness
  fields explicitly mention
  $m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$, $m_L(U)$, $m_R(U)$, the concrete cross instance
  $(U_L,U_R)$, the returned cross candidate, and the reconstructed candidate.
  It is rejected if it is only the implication
  $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }\gamma\text{-}\LSD}\to
  \TSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\LSD}$.

  The threshold transfer record binds the hard threshold in the algorithm type.
  It must define
  \[
    \operatorname{thresholdFamilyAt}(n,\ell,t)
      := \operatorname{LSDThresholdFamily}(n,\ell,t)
  \]
  and its `existsHardThreshold' projection has exactly the type
  \[
    \exists t:\R,\ 0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \NoTSQAlg{\operatorname{thresholdFamilyAt}(n,\ell,t)}.
  \]
  The same bound variable $t$ must occur in the family argument. A field of type
  $\exists t,\ 0\le t\le1\wedge
  \NoTSQAlg{\operatorname{def\_lsd\_dec.family}}$, or any conclusion whose
  family expression is independent of $t$, is a statement about an
  uninstantiated family and fails this corollary. The threshold search
  algorithm must also be exposed by projections
  `thresholdSearchRun',
  `thresholdSearchCorrectness', and `thresholdSearchRuntimeDef', with
  `thresholdSearchRun' querying the decision oracle only at values from
  $\mathcal T_\ell$ and returning an index pair attaining the least feasible
  threshold.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{thm:gamma-lsd-hardness, lem:lsd-exact-to-gamma-one-transfer, lem:lsd-larger-dimension-transfer, lem:lsd-bichromatic-transfer, lem:lsd-hard-threshold-transfer, def:no-tsq-alg, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  The logarithmic-slice $\gamma$-LSD hardness is
  Theorem~\ref{thm:gamma-lsd-hardness}.  Lemma~\ref{lem:lsd-exact-to-gamma-one-transfer}
  transfers this to exact LSD, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:lsd-larger-dimension-transfer} extends the lower bound from
  the logarithmic slice to all larger dimensions.  The bichromatic variant is
  handled by Lemma~\ref{lem:lsd-bichromatic-transfer}.  Finally,
  Lemma~\ref{lem:lsd-hard-threshold-transfer} gives the existential hard
  threshold $t\in[0,1]$ for the concrete decision family $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[First transfer in the $\gamma$-MSD hardness chain]
  \label{lem:gamma-msd-hardness-tensor-transfer}
  \uses{lem:msd-tensor-reduction, def:gamma-msd, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  If there is a truly subquadratic algorithm for
  $\gamma\text{-}\MSD_{n,\msdHardDim(c,n)}$ with
  $\msdHardGammaAllowed(C_\gamma,n,\gamma)$, then for every constant $k>0$
  there is a truly subquadratic algorithm for
  $\mildMsdGamma(n)\text{-}\MSD_{n,\polylogDim(k,n)}$.
  This node owns only the tensor-amplification transfer.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:msd-tensor-reduction}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:msd-tensor-reduction} with the hard dimension and the
  fixed polylogarithmic approximation regime. The tensor-power construction and
  approximation-root calculation are already contained in that lemma.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Second transfer in the $\gamma$-MSD hardness chain]
  \label{lem:gamma-msd-hardness-additive-msd-transfer}
  \uses{lem:msd-to-additive-msd, def:additive-msd, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  If there is a truly subquadratic algorithm for
  $\mildMsdGamma(n)\text{-}\MSD_{n,\polylogDim(k,n)}$ for every constant $k>0$,
  then there is a truly subquadratic algorithm for bichromatic
  \[
    \frac{\logn(n)}{\logDim(c,n)}
    \text{-Additive-}\MSD_{n,\logDim(c,n)}
  \]
  for every constant $c>0$. This node owns only the passage to the additive-MSD
  promise problem.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:msd-to-additive-msd}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:msd-to-additive-msd}. Its proof already packages the
  cited Karthik--Manurangsi reduction together with the additive-MSD/Max-IP
  equivalence.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Third transfer in the $\gamma$-MSD hardness chain]
  \label{lem:gamma-msd-hardness-additive-maxip-transfer}
  \uses{lem:additive-msd-maxip-equiv, def:additive-msd, def:additive-maxip, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  A truly subquadratic algorithm for bichromatic
  $\frac{\logn(n)}{\logDim(c,n)}$-Additive-$\MSD_{n,\logDim(c,n)}$ yields a
  truly subquadratic algorithm for bichromatic
  $\logn(n)$-Additive-Max-IP in logarithmic dimension. This node owns only the
  use of the additive-MSD/Additive-Max-IP equivalence inside the hardness chain.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:additive-msd-maxip-equiv}
  Project the Additive-MSD to Additive-Max-IP direction from
  Lemma~\ref{lem:additive-msd-maxip-equiv}. The padding and runtime accounting
  needed for this projection are part of that equivalence node.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Additive Max-IP algorithm would refute OVC]
  \label{lem:gamma-msd-hardness-ov-contradiction}
  \uses{thm:additive-bmaxip-to-ov, conjecture:ovc, thm:seth-implies-ovc, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  A truly subquadratic algorithm for bichromatic
  $\logn(n)$-Additive-Max-IP in dimension $\logDim(c,n)$ gives a truly
  subquadratic algorithm for $\OV_{n,\logDim(c',n)}$ for the logarithmic slice
  supplied by OVC, contradicting OVC and therefore also SETH.
  This node owns only the final contradiction step in the hardness chain.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{thm:additive-bmaxip-to-ov, conjecture:ovc, thm:seth-implies-ovc}
  Apply the imported Chen theorem
  Theorem~\ref{thm:additive-bmaxip-to-ov} to the additive Max-IP algorithm. The
  resulting truly subquadratic OV algorithm contradicts
  Conjecture~\ref{conjecture:ovc}; under SETH, use
  Theorem~\ref{thm:seth-implies-ovc} first.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Hardness of polylog-approximate $\gamma$-MSD, Theorem 1.2 from Theorem 3.3 / B.1]
  \label{thm:gamma-msd-hardness}
  \uses{def:gamma-msd, assumption:seth, conjecture:ovc, def:no-tsq-alg, def:log-parameter-regimes, lem:gamma-msd-hardness-tensor-transfer, lem:gamma-msd-hardness-additive-msd-transfer, lem:gamma-msd-hardness-additive-maxip-transfer, lem:gamma-msd-hardness-ov-contradiction}
  Assuming SETH or OVC, for every $\eps>0$ and every fixed
  $C_\gamma>0$ there exists a constant $c>0$ such that
  $\NoTSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\MSD_{n,\msdHardDim(c,n)}}$ whenever
  $\msdHardGammaAllowed(C_\gamma,n,\gamma)$, i.e.
  \[
    \ell = \msdHardDim(c,n)
      = \left\lceil n^{\frac{c}{\log\log n}}\right\rceil
    \quad\text{and}\quad
    1\le\gamma\le(\log n)^{C_\gamma}.
  \]
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:gamma-msd-hardness-tensor-transfer, lem:gamma-msd-hardness-additive-msd-transfer, lem:gamma-msd-hardness-additive-maxip-transfer, lem:gamma-msd-hardness-ov-contradiction, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  Assume a truly subquadratic algorithm for
  $\gamma\text{-}\MSD_{n,\msdHardDim(c,n)}$ in the allowed fixed-polylogarithmic
  approximation regime. Lemma~\ref{lem:gamma-msd-hardness-tensor-transfer}
  gives the mild-approximation MSD algorithm in polylogarithmic dimension.
  Lemma~\ref{lem:gamma-msd-hardness-additive-msd-transfer} turns that into a
  truly subquadratic algorithm for bichromatic additive MSD on the logarithmic
  slice, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:gamma-msd-hardness-additive-maxip-transfer} turns the latter
  into bichromatic additive Max-IP. Finally
  Lemma~\ref{lem:gamma-msd-hardness-ov-contradiction} contradicts OVC, and
  under SETH first uses the implication from SETH to OVC. Therefore no such
  $\gamma$-MSD algorithm exists.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Hardness of MSD and its variants, Corollary 3.4]
  \label{cor:msd-hardness}
  \uses{def:msd, def:gamma-msd, def:msd-dec, assumption:seth, conjecture:ovc, def:no-tsq-alg, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  Assuming SETH or OVC, for every $\eps>0$ there exists a constant $c>0$ such
  that $\NoTSQAlg{\MSD_{n,\ell}}$ when
  $\ell \ge \msdHardDim(c,n)$. Moreover the same lower bound holds for
  bichromatic $\gamma\text{-}\MSD_{n,\ell}$ whenever, for some fixed
  $C_\gamma>0$, $\msdHardGammaAllowed(C_\gamma,n,\gamma)$ holds, and for
  $\MSD_{n,\ell,t}$ for some $t \in [0,1]$.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{thm:gamma-msd-hardness, def:msd, def:msd-dec, def:no-tsq-alg, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  As in Corollary~\ref{cor:lsd-hardness}: $\gamma\text{-}\MSD$ and bichromatic
  $\gamma\text{-}\MSD$ are easier than $\MSD$, so the bound of
  Theorem~\ref{thm:gamma-msd-hardness} transfers; and for the decision version
  $\MSD_{n,\ell,t}$, the number of distinct relevant thresholds $t$ is
  $\bigO(\ell^{3})$, so a truly subquadratic algorithm for all $t$ would solve
  $\MSD_{n,\ell}$ by binary search, contradicting
  Theorem~\ref{thm:gamma-msd-hardness}; hence some $t$ is hard.
\end{proof}

\chapter{Proof of the $\gamma$-MSD hardness (Appendix B)}

\begin{definition}[Bichromatic $\gamma$-Additive-MSD]
  \label{def:additive-msd}
  \uses{def:cosine, def:log-parameter-regimes, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and additive gap $\gamma\ge 0$, an instance of
  bichromatic $\gamma$-Additive-MSD consists of two $n$-tuples
  $A=(a_1,\ldots,a_n)$ and $B=(b_1,\ldots,b_n)$ of nonzero vectors in
  $\{0,1\}^{\ell}$ and a threshold $\alpha \in [0,1]$. Let
  $c_I(i,j)=\cossim{a_i}{b_j}$. This is a promise decision family whose two
  predicates are:
  \[
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\gamma}(I)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists\,i,j,\ c_I(i,j)\ge\alpha,
  \]
  and
  \[
    \operatorname{No}_{\gamma}(I)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \forall\,i,j,\ c_I(i,j)<\alpha-\gamma.
  \]
  A solver for this promise problem must output true on every yes instance and
  false on every no instance; inputs satisfying neither predicate lie in the
  promise gap and need not be classified. The additive gap $\gamma$ appears
  specifically in the no predicate as the separation $\alpha-\gamma$. Recording
  only the yes predicate, or treating $\gamma$ as unused metadata, omits half of
  the problem.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Bichromatic $\gamma$-Additive-Max-IP]
  \label{def:additive-maxip}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:log-parameter-regimes, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and additive gap $\gamma\ge 0$, an instance of
  bichromatic $\gamma$-Additive-Max-IP ($\gamma$-Additive-BMax-IP) consists of
  two $n$-tuples $A=(a_1,\ldots,a_n)$ and $B=(b_1,\ldots,b_n)$ in
  $\{0,1\}^{\ell}$ and a threshold $\alpha$. Let
  $s_I(i,j)=\inner{a_i}{b_j}$. This is a promise decision family whose two
  predicates are:
  \[
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\gamma}(I)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists\,i,j,\ s_I(i,j)\ge\alpha,
  \]
  and
  \[
    \operatorname{No}_{\gamma}(I)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \forall\,i,j,\ s_I(i,j)<\alpha-\gamma.
  \]
  A solver must output true on all yes instances and false on all no instances;
  inputs in the gap between $\alpha-\gamma$ and $\alpha$ are outside the promise.
  The formal problem must store both vector lists, the threshold $\alpha$, both
  predicates, and the additive gap $\gamma$. A declaration containing only the
  existential yes predicate is not the additive-gap problem used by Lemma B.6.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Tensoring amplifies the MSD approximation factor, Lemma B.2]
  \label{lem:msd-tensor-reduction}
  \uses{def:gamma-msd, def:kron-power, lem:kron-power-cosine, def:tsq-alg-exists, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  Suppose $\TSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\MSD_{n,\ell}}$ holds with
  $\ell = \msdHardDim(c,n)$ for any constant $c>0$ and
  $\msdHardGammaAllowed(C_\gamma,n,\gamma)$ for some fixed $C_\gamma>0$,
  running in $\bigO(n^{2-\eps})$ time for any $\eps>0$. Then
  $\TSQAlg{\mildMsdGamma(n)\text{-}\MSD_{n,\polylogDim(k,n)}}$ holds with the
  same truly subquadratic exponent for any constant $k>0$.

  The declaration audited at this label must expose the concrete reduction
  package $\operatorname{MSDTensorAmplificationWitness}$. The package contains
  the following data, equations and correctness fields; it is not a proposition
  comparing two copies of `def_gamma_msd.family'.
  First it defines the tensor exponent
  \[
    q(n)=\left\lceil\frac{\log n}{(\log\log n)^2}\right\rceil
  \]
  and, for an input instance
  $V=(v_1,\ldots,v_n)$ of
  $\mildMsdGamma(n)$-$\MSD_{n,\polylogDim(k,n)}$, the concrete target instance
  \[
    \operatorname{tensorInst}(V)
      = (v_1^{\otimes q(n)},\ldots,v_n^{\otimes q(n)}).
  \]
  Its row equation is a required projection:
  \[
    \operatorname{tensorInst\_row}(V,i):
      \operatorname{tensorInst}(V)_i=v_i^{\otimes q(n)}.
  \]
  The target dimension is also a projection, not a comment:
  \[
    \operatorname{tensorDim}(k,n)=\polylogDim(k,n)^{q(n)}
  \]
  together with the asymptotic hard-dimension comparison
  \[
    \operatorname{tensorDimBound}:
      \operatorname{tensorDim}(k,n)
      \le \msdHardDim(c',n)
  \]
  for a constant $c'$ depending only on $k$ and the fixed ceiling convention.
  The witness must include the Kronecker-power cosine equation
  \[
    \operatorname{tensorCosine}(V,i,j):
      \cossim{\operatorname{tensorInst}(V)_i}
             {\operatorname{tensorInst}(V)_j}
      =
      \bigl(\cossim{v_i}{v_j}\bigr)^{q(n)}
  \]
  by Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-cosine}.

  The approximation-transfer field is the real content of the lemma. If a
  target oracle returns a pair $o=(i,j)$ satisfying
  \[
    \Gamma(n)^{-1}M_{\operatorname{tensorInst}(V)}
      \le
      \cossim{\operatorname{tensorInst}(V)_i}
             {\operatorname{tensorInst}(V)_j}
      \le
      M_{\operatorname{tensorInst}(V)}
  \]
  with $\Gamma(n)\le(\log n)^{C_\gamma}$, then the same pair is returned for
  $V$ and the witness proves
  \[
    \mildMsdGamma(n)^{-1}M_V
      \le \cossim{v_i}{v_j}\le M_V.
  \]
  This proof must use
  $\operatorname{tensorCosine}$, monotonicity of powers on $[0,1]$, and the
  root bound
  \[
    \operatorname{gammaRootBound}:
      \Gamma(n)^{1/q(n)}
      \le 1+\frac{1}{\log\log n}
      =\mildMsdGamma(n)
  \]
  for all sufficiently large $n$. A field named `tensorMapStatement' whose
  content is an identity on `Fin 1', or a transfer implication between
  identical $\operatorname{def\_gamma\_msd.family}$ algorithm types, is
  rejected.

  The runtime transfer is also part of the node. The package defines
  \[
    \operatorname{tensorReductionRuntime}(T_{\gamma\MSD},n,k,\gamma)
      =
      c_{\mathrm{build}}\,n\,\operatorname{tensorDim}(k,n)
      +
      c_{\mathrm{call}}T_{\gamma\MSD}
        (n,\operatorname{tensorDim}(k,n),\gamma)
      +c_{\mathrm{return}},
  \]
  proves a bound by the displayed expression, and proves an
  exponent-preservation theorem: if the target runtime is
  $O(n^{2-\eps})$ on the hard dimension with fixed polylogarithmic
  approximation regime, then
  $\operatorname{tensorReductionRuntime}$ is
  $O(n^{2-\eps'})$ for some $\eps'>0$ after absorbing the
  $n\,\operatorname{tensorDim}(k,n)$ construction cost into the
  subquadratic slack for the chosen hard-dimension constant. The accepted
  witness therefore has projections named, or transparently equivalent to,
  `q', `tensorInst', `tensorInst_row', `tensorDim',
  `tensorDimBound', `tensorCosine', `gammaRootBound',
  `approximationTransfer', `tensorReductionRuntime',
  `tensorReductionRuntimeDef', and `tensorRuntimeTsq'. None of these may be
  replaced by `True', a `Fin 1' identity, or an implication between identical
  algorithm-existence propositions.

  Trial-8 alignment requirement: the field `q' is the tensor exponent
  \[
    q(n)=\left\lceil\frac{\log n}{(\log\log n)^2}\right\rceil
  \]
  and the witness must contain the projection
  \[
    \operatorname{q\_eq}(n):
    q(n)=\left\lceil\frac{\log n}{(\log\log n)^2}\right\rceil .
  \]
  A generated definition `q n = n+1', or any exponent not asymptotic to the
  displayed ratio, is not this lemma. The target dimension field is
  \[
    \operatorname{tensorDim}(k,n)
      =\polylogDim(k,n)^{q(n)},
  \]
  with projection `tensorDim_eq'; it is not $n+1$ and it is not the original
  source dimension. The target oracle call in `tensorReductionRuntimeDef' must
  be
  \[
    T_{\gamma\MSD}(n,\operatorname{tensorDim}(k,n),\gamma),
  \]
  not $T_{\gamma\MSD}(n,n+1,\gamma)$ and not an unindexed call to
  `def_gamma_msd.family'.

  The root-bound field has the indexed form
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{gammaRootBound}:\\
    \qquad
    \forall C_\gamma>0,\ \exists n_0,\ \forall n\ge n_0,\ \forall\gamma,\ 
    \msdHardGammaAllowed(C_\gamma,n,\gamma)\to
    \gamma^{1/q(n)}
      \le 1+\frac{1}{\log\log n}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  It is not the statement $\gamma\le\logn(n)^{-1}$, nor any formula involving
  $\mildMsdGamma(n)=\logn(n)^{-1}$. The field `tensorRuntimeTsq' is an
  exponent-preservation theorem about the named
  $\operatorname{tensorReductionRuntime}$:
  from a target runtime bound on the hard-dimension family it constructs a
  source runtime bound for
  $\mildMsdGamma(n)$-$\MSD_{n,\polylogDim(k,n)}$ with some $\eps'>0$. It is
  rejected if its type is an implication between identical
  $\operatorname{def\_tsq\_alg\_exists}$ propositions, or if neither
  $\operatorname{tensorDim}(k,n)$ nor
  $\operatorname{tensorReductionRuntime}$ occurs in the statement.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:kron-power-cosine, def:gamma-msd, def:kron-power, def:cosine, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  Let $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in \{0,1\}^{\polylogDim(k,n)}$ be an instance of
  $\mildMsdGamma(n)\text{-}\MSD_{n,\polylogDim(k,n)}$. Construct
  $V' = \{v_1^{\otimes q}, \ldots, v_n^{\otimes q}\}$ for
  $q = \frac{\log n}{(\log\log n)^{2}}$. The vectors of $V'$ have dimension
  \[
    (\log n)^{kq}
      =(\log n)^{\frac{k\log n}{(\log\log n)^2}}
      =n^{\frac{k}{\log\log n}},
  \]
  so, up to the fixed ceiling convention and a harmless renaming of the constant
  $c$, this is exactly the hard dimension
  $\msdHardDim(k,n)=\lceil n^{k/\log\log n}\rceil$. Run the assumed hard-regime
  algorithm on $V'$ with any fixed polylogarithmic approximation factor
  $\Gamma(n)=(\log n)^{C_\gamma}$ satisfying
  $\msdHardGammaAllowed(C_\gamma,n,\Gamma(n))$. By
  Lemma~\ref{lem:kron-power-cosine},
  \[
    \frac{\inner{v_i^{\otimes q}}{v_j^{\otimes q}}}
         {\norm{v_i^{\otimes q}}\cdot\norm{v_j^{\otimes q}}}
    = \left(\cossim{v_i}{v_j}\right)^{q}
  \]
  for all $i,j$. Therefore a $\Gamma(n)$-approximation of MSD on $V'$ is a
  $\Gamma(n)^{1/q}$-approximation of MSD on $v_1,\ldots,v_n$. Since
  \[
    \Gamma(n)^{1/q}
      =(\log n)^{C_\gamma(\log\log n)^2/\log n}
      \le 1+\frac{1}{\log\log n}
      =\mildMsdGamma(n)
  \]
  for all sufficiently large $n$, the returned pair is also a valid
  $\mildMsdGamma(n)$-approximation. The running time is preserved up to the
  $\bigO(n^{2-\eps})$ bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Karthik--Manurangsi reduction, Theorem B.4]
  \label{thm:additive-maxip-karthik}
  \uses{def:gamma-msd, def:additive-maxip, def:tsq-alg-exists, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  This is the cited Theorem 6.2 of Karthik--Manurangsi (2020), used by the paper
  without reproducing the graph-construction proof. Its content is:
  Suppose
  $\TSQAlg{\mildMsdGamma(n)\text{-}\MSD_{n,\polylogDim(k,n)}}$ holds for any
  constant $k>0$ and any truly subquadratic exponent. Then
  $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }\logn(n)\text{-Additive-Max-IP}_{n,\logDim(c,n)}}$
  holds for any constant $c>0$ with some positive truly subquadratic exponent.
  A disposable Lean implementation should treat this node as an axiom/imported
  external theorem unless it formalizes the full graph construction and its
  approximation-gap analysis.

  The imported theorem is still an indexed, parameter-sensitive statement. The
  declaration audited at this label must be an axiom or theorem package
  $\operatorname{KarthikManurangsiB4}$ with projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{sourceFamily}(k):&
      \mildMsdGamma(n)\text{-}\MSD_{n,\polylogDim(k,n)},\\
    \operatorname{targetFamily}(c):&
      \text{bichromatic }\logn(n)\text{-Additive-Max-IP}_{n,\logDim(c,n)},\\
    \operatorname{sourceApproxEq}:&
      \mildMsdGamma(n)=1+\frac{1}{\log\log n},\\
    \operatorname{sourceDimEq}:&
      \polylogDim(k,n)=\lceil(\log n)^k\rceil,\\
    \operatorname{targetGapEq}:&
      \text{additive gap}=\logn(n),\\
    \operatorname{targetDimEq}:&
      \text{target dimension}=\logDim(c,n),\\
    \operatorname{exponentTransfer}:&
      \forall \eps>0,\ \exists \eps'>0,\ 
      \TSQAlg{\operatorname{sourceFamily}(k)}
      \Rightarrow
      \TSQAlg{\operatorname{targetFamily}(c)}
      \text{ with exponent }\eps'.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The target family must be the bichromatic additive Max-IP promise family of
  Definition~\ref{def:additive-maxip}, with two color classes, threshold
  $\alpha$, yes predicate $\exists i,j,\inner{a_i}{b_j}\ge\alpha$, no predicate
  $\forall i,j,\inner{a_i}{b_j}<\alpha-\logn(n)$, and dimension
  $\logDim(c,n)$. A theorem whose type is only an unparameterized implication
  \[
    \operatorname{def\_tsq\_alg\_exists}(P)\to
    \operatorname{def\_tsq\_alg\_exists}(Q)
  \]
  for generic family values $P,Q$ is not this imported result. The
  approximation factor, the source dimension $\polylogDim(k,n)$, the
  bichromatic target, the additive gap $\logn(n)$, the logarithmic target
  dimension, and the positive target exponent must all occur in the audited
  statement.

  Trial-8 alignment requirement: this imported theorem package must not use the
  uninstantiated family values `def_gamma_msd.family' and
  `def_additive_maxip.family' as its source and target. It has indexed family
  constructors
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{sourceFamily}(k,n):&
      \gamma\text{-}\MSD\text{ instantiated at }
      (n,\polylogDim(k,n),\mildMsdGamma(n)),\\
    \operatorname{targetFamily}(c,n):&
      \text{bichromatic additive Max-IP instantiated at }
      (n,\logDim(c,n),\logn(n)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The projection equations are part of the axiom package:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{sourceApproxEq}(n):&
      \mildMsdGamma(n)=1+\frac{1}{\log\log n},\\
    \operatorname{sourceDimEq}(k,n):&
      \polylogDim(k,n)=\lceil(\log n)^k\rceil,\\
    \operatorname{targetGapEq}(n):&
      \operatorname{targetGap}(n)=\logn(n),\\
    \operatorname{targetDimEq}(c,n):&
      \operatorname{targetDim}(c,n)=\logDim(c,n).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The statement
  $\operatorname{sourceApproxEq}:\mildMsdGamma(n)=\logn(n)^{-1}$ is explicitly
  wrong for this paper and fails the node. The algorithm-transfer field is
  parameterized by $k,c,\eps$ and produces an $\eps'>0$ for the indexed target
  family:
  \[
    \forall k,c,\eps>0,\ \exists\eps'>0,\quad
    \TSQAlg{\operatorname{sourceFamily}(k,n)}
    \Rightarrow
    \TSQAlg{\operatorname{targetFamily}(c,n)}.
  \]
  Both occurrences of $\TSQAlg$ must mention these indexed constructors, and
  the target family must unfold to the promise problem with yes predicate
  $\exists i,j,\inner{a_i}{b_j}\ge\alpha$ and no predicate
  $\forall i,j,\inner{a_i}{b_j}<\alpha-\logn(n)$. A generic transfer between
  arbitrary problem-family variables, or a transfer between the two bare
  `.family' fields, erases Theorem B.4's mathematical content.
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Equal-weight padding for additive MSD/Max-IP]
  \label{def:additive-msd-maxip-padding}
  \uses{def:additive-msd, def:additive-maxip}
  For a binary vector $a_i\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$ define
  \[
    a_i'=
    a_i\circ 1^{\ell-\norm{a_i}_1}\circ
    0^{\ell+\norm{a_i}_1}\in\{0,1\}^{3\ell},
  \]
  and for a binary vector $b_j\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$ define
  \[
    b_j'=
    b_j\circ 0^{\ell+\norm{b_j}_1}\circ
    1^{\ell-\norm{b_j}_1}\in\{0,1\}^{3\ell}.
  \]
  For bichromatic sets $A,B$, write
  $\operatorname{padA}(A)=A'$ and $\operatorname{padB}(B)=B'$ for the row-wise
  padded sets. This node owns only the concrete padding maps and their output
  dimension $3\ell$.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Padded additive instances have uniform norm]
  \label{lem:additive-padding-uniform-norm}
  \uses{def:additive-msd, def:additive-msd-maxip-padding, def:l2norm}
  For every padded row $a_i'$ or $b_j'$ from
  Definition~\ref{def:additive-msd-maxip-padding},
  \[
    \norm{a_i'}=\sqrt{\ell},
    \qquad
    \norm{b_j'}=\sqrt{\ell}.
  \]
  Equivalently, every padded row has exactly $\ell$ one entries.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:additive-msd-maxip-padding, def:l2norm}
  The row $a_i'$ contains the original $\norm{a_i}_1$ one entries plus
  $\ell-\norm{a_i}_1$ appended one entries, and the remaining appended entries
  are zero. Thus it has exactly $\ell$ ones. The same count for $b_j'$ uses its
  final block of $\ell-\norm{b_j}_1$ ones. For binary vectors, the Euclidean
  norm is the square root of the number of one entries, giving the two displayed
  norm equations.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Padded additive instances preserve cross inner products]
  \label{lem:additive-padding-preserves-inner}
  \uses{def:additive-msd-maxip-padding, def:inner-prod}
  For every original cross pair $(a_i,b_j)$ and its padded pair
  $(a_i',b_j')$,
  \[
    \inner{a_i'}{b_j'}=\inner{a_i}{b_j}.
  \]
  This node owns only the inner-product preservation equation.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:additive-msd-maxip-padding, def:inner-prod}
  The first $\ell$ coordinates contribute $\inner{a_i}{b_j}$. In the appended
  coordinates the extra ones of $a_i'$ occur only in the block where $b_j'$ has
  zeros, and the extra ones of $b_j'$ occur only in the block where $a_i'$ has
  zeros. Hence the appended coordinates contribute $0$, so the cross inner
  product is preserved.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Additive-Max-IP gaps transfer to padded Additive-MSD gaps]
  \label{lem:additive-maxip-gap-to-msd-gap}
  \uses{def:additive-msd, def:additive-maxip, lem:additive-padding-uniform-norm, lem:additive-padding-preserves-inner, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  Let $A,B,\alpha$ be a bichromatic
  $\logn(n)$-Additive-Max-IP instance. After applying the padding of
  Definition~\ref{def:additive-msd-maxip-padding}, the Additive-MSD threshold
  $\alpha/\ell$ and additive gap $\logn(n)/\ell$ distinguish the corresponding
  yes and no cases:
  \[
    \exists a,b,\ \inner{a}{b}\ge\alpha
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists a',b',\ \cossim{a'}{b'}\ge\frac{\alpha}{\ell},
  \]
  and
  \[
    \forall a,b,\ \inner{a}{b}<\alpha-\logn(n)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \forall a',b',\
      \cossim{a'}{b'}<
      \frac{\alpha}{\ell}-\frac{\logn(n)}{\ell}.
  \]
  This node owns only the promise-gap correctness for the Max-IP to MSD
  direction.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:additive-padding-uniform-norm, lem:additive-padding-preserves-inner, def:cosine}
  For every cross pair, Lemma~\ref{lem:additive-padding-preserves-inner} gives
  the numerator equality and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:additive-padding-uniform-norm} gives
  $\norm{a'}\norm{b'}=\ell$. Therefore
  $\cossim{a'}{b'}=\inner{a}{b}/\ell$. Dividing the yes threshold and no-gap
  threshold by the positive scalar $\ell$ gives the two equivalences.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Additive-MSD gaps transfer to padded Additive-Max-IP gaps]
  \label{lem:additive-msd-gap-to-maxip-gap}
  \uses{def:additive-msd, def:additive-maxip, lem:additive-padding-uniform-norm, lem:additive-padding-preserves-inner, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  Let $A,B,\alpha$ be a bichromatic
  $\frac{\logn(n)}{\ell}$-Additive-MSD instance. After applying the same padding,
  an Additive-Max-IP solver at threshold $\alpha\ell$ and additive gap
  $\logn(n)$ distinguishes the corresponding yes and no cases:
  \[
    \exists a,b,\ \cossim{a}{b}\ge\alpha
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists a',b',\ \inner{a'}{b'}\ge\alpha\ell,
  \]
  and the no promise with separation $\logn(n)/\ell$ transfers to
  \[
    \forall a',b',\ \inner{a'}{b'}<\alpha\ell-\logn(n).
  \]
  This node owns only the promise-gap correctness for the MSD to Max-IP
  direction.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:additive-padding-uniform-norm, lem:additive-padding-preserves-inner, def:cosine}
  The same pairwise calculation gives
  $\cossim{a'}{b'}=\inner{a}{b}/\ell$ for padded rows. Multiplying the MSD yes
  threshold and no threshold by the positive scalar $\ell$ gives exactly the
  Additive-Max-IP thresholds $\alpha\ell$ and $\alpha\ell-\logn(n)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Runtime accounting for additive padding reductions]
  \label{lem:additive-padding-runtime}
  \uses{def:fg-reduction-predicates, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  In both padding directions, constructing the padded bichromatic instance,
  running the target oracle once, and returning the same Boolean answer has
  runtime
  \[
    T_{\mathrm{pad}}(n,\ell)
    =
    c_{\mathrm{build}}\,n\ell+
    c_{\mathrm{call}}\,T_{\mathrm{target}}(n,3\ell)+
    c_{\mathrm{return}},
  \]
  and hence
  \[
    T_{\mathrm{pad}}(n,\ell)
    \le C\bigl(n\ell+T_{\mathrm{target}}(n,3\ell)\bigr).
  \]
  On the slice $\ell=O(\log n)$, this preserves a positive truly subquadratic
  exponent up to polynomial factors in $\ell$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:fg-reduction-predicates, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  Building $2n$ padded rows of dimension $3\ell$ takes $O(n\ell)$ time. The
  reduction then makes exactly one target oracle call and only rescales the
  threshold and returns the Boolean answer. Since replacing $\ell$ by $3\ell$
  changes only the polynomial-in-$\ell$ factor on the logarithmic slice, the
  target truly subquadratic exponent is preserved, possibly after decreasing it
  by a constant amount to absorb the lower-order build cost.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Additive-MSD is equivalent to Additive-Max-IP, Lemma B.5]
  \label{lem:additive-msd-maxip-equiv}
  \uses{def:additive-msd, def:additive-maxip, def:fg-reduction-predicates, def:log-parameter-regimes, def:additive-msd-maxip-padding, lem:additive-maxip-gap-to-msd-gap, lem:additive-msd-gap-to-maxip-gap, lem:additive-padding-runtime}
  $\SubquadEquiv{\text{bichromatic }\frac{\logn(n)}{\ell}\text{-Additive-}\MSD_{n,\ell}}
  {\text{bichromatic }\logn(n)\text{-Additive-Max-IP}_{n,\ell'}}$ when
  $\ell = \bigO(\log n)$ and $\ell' = \bigO(\log n)$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:additive-msd-maxip-padding, lem:additive-maxip-gap-to-msd-gap, lem:additive-msd-gap-to-maxip-gap, lem:additive-padding-runtime}
  Use the padding maps of Definition~\ref{def:additive-msd-maxip-padding}. The
  direction from Additive-Max-IP to Additive-MSD is exactly the promise-gap
  transfer of Lemma~\ref{lem:additive-maxip-gap-to-msd-gap}; the converse
  direction is exactly Lemma~\ref{lem:additive-msd-gap-to-maxip-gap}. In both
  directions the runtime is the one-call padding runtime of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:additive-padding-runtime}, so the reductions preserve truly
  subquadratic time on logarithmic dimensions. These two reductions give the
  displayed subquadratic equivalence.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Bichromatic Additive-MSD reduces to Additive-Max-IP, Lemma B.3]
  \label{lem:msd-to-additive-msd}
  \uses{def:gamma-msd, def:additive-msd, def:additive-maxip, def:tsq-alg-exists, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  If
  $\TSQAlg{\mildMsdGamma(n)\text{-}\MSD_{n,\polylogDim(k,n)}}$ holds for any
  constant $k>0$, then
  $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }\frac{\logn(n)}{\logDim(c,n)}\text{-Additive-}
  \MSD_{n,\logDim(c,n)}}$ holds for any $c>0$ with some positive truly
  subquadratic exponent.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{thm:additive-maxip-karthik, lem:additive-msd-maxip-equiv, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  By Theorem~\ref{thm:additive-maxip-karthik}, the assumed
  $\mildMsdGamma(n)$-MSD algorithm yields a truly subquadratic algorithm for
  bichromatic $\logn(n)$-Additive-Max-IP. By
  Lemma~\ref{lem:additive-msd-maxip-equiv}, bichromatic $\logn(n)$-Additive-
  Max-IP is subquadratic equivalent to bichromatic
  $\frac{\logn(n)}{\ell}$-Additive-MSD, so the latter is also truly
  subquadratic.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Additive-BMax-IP refutes OVC, Lemma B.6 (Chen 2020)]
  \label{thm:additive-bmaxip-to-ov}
  \uses{def:additive-maxip, def:ov, conjecture:ovc, assumption:seth, def:tsq-alg-exists, def:log-parameter-regimes}
