  This is a cited external dependency from Chen (2020), not a proof reproduced
  in this paper. Its content is:
  If $\TSQAlg{\logn(n)\text{-Additive-BMax-IP}_{n,\logDim(c,n)}}$ holds for any
  constant $c>0$ with some positive truly subquadratic exponent, then
  $\TSQAlg{\OV_{n,\logDim(c',n)}}$ holds for any constant $c'>0$ with some
  positive truly subquadratic exponent, refuting SETH and OVC.
  A formalization may register this as an axiom/imported theorem. It should not
  attempt to prove this node from the definitions alone unless it also
  formalizes Chen's additive maximum-inner-product hardness theorem.
\end{assumption}

\chapter{Representational strength of transformers}

\begin{lemma}[OV attention row formula]
  \label{lem:attention-ov-row-formula}
  \uses{def:attention, def:softmax, def:ov, def:inner-prod}
  In the OV construction with $v_{n+1}=0^\ell$,
  $M_{Q,K}=-3\log n\cdot I_\ell$, all-one value matrix
  $V\in\R^{\ell\times1}$, and identity input MLP, the $i$-th scalar output of
  the attention unit is
  \[
    \frac{\sum_{j=1}^{n} n^{-3\inner{v_i}{v_j}}\cdot \norm{v_j}_1}
           {\sum_{k=1}^{n} n^{-3\inner{v_i}{v_k}} + 1}.
  \]
  This node owns only the attention-entry expansion and the softmax exponential
  rewrite.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:attention, def:softmax, def:inner-prod}
  Expand Definition~\ref{def:attention}. The score of row $i$ against row $j$
  is $-3\log n\cdot\inner{v_i}{v_j}$, while the appended zero row contributes
  $\exp(0)=1$ to the denominator and value $0$. The all-one value matrix maps
  each original row $v_j$ to $\norm{v_j}_1$. Rewriting
  $\exp(-3\log n\cdot r)$ as $n^{-3r}$ gives the displayed fraction.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[OV yes instances create a large attention entry]
  \label{lem:attention-ov-yes-gap}
  \uses{lem:attention-ov-row-formula, def:ov, def:inner-prod}
  In the OV attention construction, if there exist $i^*\ne j^*$ with
  $\inner{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}}=0$, then some scalar output entry of the attention
  unit is at least
  \[
    \frac{1}{n+1}.
  \]
  This node owns only the lower-bound part of the gap analysis.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-ov-row-formula}
  Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-ov-row-formula} to row $i^*$. The numerator
  contains the term
  $n^{-3\inner{v_{i^*}}{v_{j^*}}}\norm{v_{j^*}}_1=\norm{v_{j^*}}_1$, and the
  denominator is at most $n+1$ because all original softmax weights are at most
  $1$ in this nonpositive-score construction. Since the orthogonal partner is
  nonzero in the nontrivial OV branch, $\norm{v_{j^*}}_1\ge1$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[OV no instances make all attention entries small]
  \label{lem:attention-ov-no-gap}
  \uses{lem:attention-ov-row-formula, def:ov, def:inner-prod}
  In the OV attention construction, if $\inner{v_i}{v_j}\ge1$ for every original
  pair under consideration, then every scalar output entry of the attention unit
  is at most
  \[
    \frac{\ell}{n^2}<\frac{1}{(n+1)^{1.5}}
  \]
  in the paper's polylogarithmic dimension regime. This node owns only the
  upper-bound part of the gap analysis.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-ov-row-formula}
  The denominator in Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-ov-row-formula} is at least $1$.
  Each original summand is bounded by
  $n^{-3\inner{v_i}{v_j}}\norm{v_j}_1\le n^{-3}\ell$, and there are $n$ such
  summands. Hence the row output is at most $\ell/n^2$, which is below
  $(n+1)^{-1.5}$ on the parameter regime used by the theorem.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[OV attention gap is separated by the output MLP]
  \label{lem:attention-ov-threshold-gap}
  \uses{lem:attention-ov-yes-gap, lem:attention-ov-no-gap, lem:mlp-threshold}
  The output MLP supplied by Lemma~\ref{lem:mlp-threshold}, with lower cutoff
  $a=(n+1)^{-1.5}$ and upper cutoff $b=(n+1)^{-1}$, maps the OV attention
  output to $1$ on yes instances and to $0$ on no instances.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-ov-yes-gap, lem:attention-ov-no-gap, lem:mlp-threshold}
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-ov-yes-gap} supplies an entry at least $b$ in the yes
  case, while Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-ov-no-gap} puts every entry below $a$ in
  the no case. Lemma~\ref{lem:mlp-threshold} gives a continuous MLP separating
  these two regions.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[An attention unit solves OV, Theorem 4.1]
  \label{thm:attention-solves-ov}
  \uses{def:transformer, def:tf-solves, def:ov, def:attention-solves-predicate}
  An attention unit with input and output MLPs and parameters $d = \ell$,
  $d_{\mathrm{in}} = \ell$, $d_{\mathrm{out}} = 1$, $m \ge \ell + 1$ can solve
  $\OV_{n,\ell}$; in the notation of
  Definition~\ref{def:attention-solves-predicate}, $\AttentionSolves{\OV_{n,\ell}}$.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:tf-solves, def:ov, lem:attention-ov-row-formula, lem:attention-ov-yes-gap, lem:attention-ov-no-gap, lem:attention-ov-threshold-gap}
  Choose the identity input MLP, the all-one value matrix, and
  $Q,K$ with score bilinear form
  $M_{Q,K}=-3\log n\cdot I_\ell$.  The concrete row formula is
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-ov-row-formula}.  Lemmas
  \ref{lem:attention-ov-yes-gap} and~\ref{lem:attention-ov-no-gap} prove the
  two separated output regimes.  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-ov-threshold-gap}
  supplies the output MLP that maps those regimes to the Boolean OV answer.
  These data instantiate Definition~\ref{def:attention-solves-predicate}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Max-IP attention row formula]
  \label{lem:attention-maxip-row-formula}
  \uses{def:attention, def:softmax, def:maxip-dec, lem:mlp-append, def:inner-prod}
  In the Max-IP decision construction, set
  $x_i=(v_i,1)$ for original rows and
  $x_{n+1}=(0,\ldots,0,t+1)$, choose
  $M_{Q,K}=3\log n\cdot I_{\ell+1}$, and use
  $\mathcal V=(1,\ldots,1,0)$.  The $i$-th scalar output of the attention unit
  is
  \[
    \frac{\sum_{j=1}^{n} n^{3\inner{x_i}{x_j}}\cdot \norm{v_j}_1}
         {\sum_{k=1}^{n} n^{3\inner{x_i}{x_k}} + n^{3(t+1)}}.
  \]
  This node owns only the Max-IP row expansion after the input MLP has appended
  the separator coordinate.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:attention, def:softmax, lem:mlp-append, def:inner-prod}
  Lemma~\ref{lem:mlp-append} supplies the rows $x_i$.  Expanding
  Definition~\ref{def:attention}, the score of row $i$ against original row
  $j$ is $3\log n\cdot\inner{x_i}{x_j}$, the special row contributes
  $\exp(3(t+1)\log n)=n^{3(t+1)}$ to the denominator, and the value matrix maps
  $x_j$ to $\norm{v_j}_1$.  Rewriting exponentials gives the displayed
  fraction.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Max-IP yes instances create a large attention entry]
  \label{lem:attention-maxip-yes-gap}
  \uses{lem:attention-maxip-row-formula, def:maxip-dec, def:inner-prod}
  In the Max-IP construction, if some distinct pair satisfies
  $\inner{v_i}{v_j}\ge t$, then some scalar output entry is at least
  $\frac{1}{n+1}$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-maxip-row-formula}
  Let $i^*,j^*$ maximize the original inner product.  The yes hypothesis gives
  $\inner{x_{i^*}}{x_{j^*}}\ge t+1$.  In the row formula, the numerator contains
  the term
  $n^{3\inner{x_{i^*}}{x_{j^*}}}\norm{v_{j^*}}_1$, and the denominator is at
  most $(n+1)n^{3\inner{x_{i^*}}{x_{j^*}}}$ because all $n$ original terms and
  the special-row term are bounded by the maximal displayed exponential.
  Since the returned partner has $\norm{v_{j^*}}_1\ge1$, the row output is at
  least $1/(n+1)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Max-IP no instances make all attention entries small]
  \label{lem:attention-maxip-no-gap}
  \uses{lem:attention-maxip-row-formula, def:maxip-dec, def:inner-prod}
  In the Max-IP construction, if $\inner{v_i}{v_j}\le t-1$ for all distinct
  original pairs, then every scalar output entry is at most
  \[
    \frac{\ell}{n^2}<\frac{1}{(n+1)^{1.5}}
  \]
  in the paper's polylogarithmic dimension regime.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-maxip-row-formula}
  Under the no hypothesis, each original off-diagonal score satisfies
  $\inner{x_i}{x_j}\le t$.  The denominator in
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-maxip-row-formula} contains the special-row term
  $n^{3(t+1)}$.  The numerator has at most $n$ original terms, each bounded by
  $n^{3t}\ell$.  Hence the output is at most
  $\ell n n^{3t}/n^{3(t+1)}=\ell/n^2$, which is below
  $(n+1)^{-1.5}$ on the stated regime.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Min-IP attention row formula]
  \label{lem:attention-minip-row-formula}
  \uses{def:attention, def:softmax, def:minip-dec, lem:mlp-append, def:inner-prod}
  In the Min-IP decision construction, set
  $x_i=(v_i,1)$ for original rows and
  $x_{n+1}=(0,\ldots,0,-(t+1))$, choose
  $M_{Q,K}=-3\log n\cdot I_{\ell+1}$, and use
  $\mathcal V=(1,\ldots,1,0)$.  The $i$-th scalar output of the attention unit
  is
  \[
    \frac{\sum_{j=1}^{n} n^{-3\inner{x_i}{x_j}}\cdot \norm{v_j}_1}
         {\sum_{k=1}^{n} n^{-3\inner{x_i}{x_k}} + n^{-3(t+1)}}.
  \]
  This node owns only the Min-IP row expansion.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:attention, def:softmax, lem:mlp-append, def:inner-prod}
  The proof is the row-formula calculation of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-maxip-row-formula} with the sign of the score
  bilinear form reversed and the special row changed to
  $(0,\ldots,0,-(t+1))$.  Thus the special-row denominator contribution is
  $n^{-3(t+1)}$ and original row $j$ contributes
  $n^{-3\inner{x_i}{x_j}}\norm{v_j}_1$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Min-IP yes instances create a large attention entry]
  \label{lem:attention-minip-yes-gap}
  \uses{lem:attention-minip-row-formula, def:minip-dec, def:inner-prod}
  In the Min-IP construction, if some distinct pair satisfies
  $\inner{v_i}{v_j}\le t$, then some scalar output entry is at least
  $\frac{1}{n+1}$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-minip-row-formula}
  Let $i^*,j^*$ minimize the augmented inner product.  The yes hypothesis gives
  $\inner{x_{i^*}}{x_{j^*}}\le t+1$.  In the row formula, the numerator contains
  a term with weight at least $n^{-3(t+1)}$, and the denominator is at most
  $n+1$ times that dominant scale after comparing all terms with the minimum.
  Since $\norm{v_{j^*}}_1\ge1$, the $i^*$-th output is at least $1/(n+1)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Min-IP no instances make all attention entries small]
  \label{lem:attention-minip-no-gap}
  \uses{lem:attention-minip-row-formula, def:minip-dec, def:inner-prod}
  In the Min-IP construction, if $\inner{v_i}{v_j}\ge t+1$ for all distinct
  original pairs, then every scalar output entry is at most
  \[
    \frac{\ell}{n^2}<\frac{1}{(n+1)^{1.5}}
  \]
  in the paper's polylogarithmic dimension regime.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-minip-row-formula}
  The no hypothesis gives $\inner{x_i}{x_j}\ge t+2$ on original off-diagonal
  pairs.  The numerator is bounded by
  $\ell n n^{-3(t+2)}$, while the special-row term in the denominator is
  $n^{-3(t+1)}$.  The quotient is at most $\ell/n^2$, and this is below
  $(n+1)^{-1.5}$ in the stated dimension regime.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Max-IP and Min-IP attention gaps are thresholded by the output MLP]
  \label{lem:attention-maxip-minip-threshold-gap}
  \uses{lem:attention-maxip-yes-gap, lem:attention-maxip-no-gap, lem:attention-minip-yes-gap, lem:attention-minip-no-gap, lem:mlp-threshold}
  The output MLP from Lemma~\ref{lem:mlp-threshold}, with lower cutoff
  $a=(n+1)^{-1.5}$ and upper cutoff $b=(n+1)^{-1}$, separates both attention
  constructions: it outputs $1$ in the corresponding yes case and $0$ in the
  corresponding no case.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-maxip-yes-gap, lem:attention-maxip-no-gap, lem:attention-minip-yes-gap, lem:attention-minip-no-gap, lem:mlp-threshold}
  The Max-IP gap is exactly Lemmas~\ref{lem:attention-maxip-yes-gap} and
  \ref{lem:attention-maxip-no-gap}; the Min-IP gap is exactly
  Lemmas~\ref{lem:attention-minip-yes-gap} and
  \ref{lem:attention-minip-no-gap}.  Lemma~\ref{lem:mlp-threshold} supplies one
  continuous thresholding MLP for the common cutoffs.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[An attention unit solves Max-IP decision]
  \label{lem:attention-solves-maxip-dec}
  \uses{def:transformer, def:tf-solves, def:maxip-dec, def:attention-solves-predicate, lem:mlp-append, lem:attention-maxip-row-formula, lem:attention-maxip-yes-gap, lem:attention-maxip-no-gap, lem:attention-maxip-minip-threshold-gap}
  With parameters $d=\ell$, $d_{\mathrm{in}}=\ell+1$,
  $d_{\mathrm{out}}=1$, and $m\ge\ell+1$, a single attention unit with input and
  output MLPs solves $\MaxIP_{n,\ell,t}$ for $1\le t\le\ell$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:mlp-append, lem:attention-maxip-row-formula, lem:attention-maxip-yes-gap, lem:attention-maxip-no-gap, lem:attention-maxip-minip-threshold-gap}
  Use Lemma~\ref{lem:mlp-append} to produce the augmented rows, choose the
  positive score bilinear form $3\log n\cdot I_{\ell+1}$ and the value vector
  $(1,\ldots,1,0)$.  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-maxip-row-formula} gives the row
  formula, Lemmas~\ref{lem:attention-maxip-yes-gap} and
  \ref{lem:attention-maxip-no-gap} prove the two cases, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-maxip-minip-threshold-gap} supplies the output MLP.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[An attention unit solves Min-IP decision]
  \label{lem:attention-solves-minip-dec}
  \uses{def:transformer, def:tf-solves, def:minip-dec, def:attention-solves-predicate, lem:mlp-append, lem:attention-minip-row-formula, lem:attention-minip-yes-gap, lem:attention-minip-no-gap, lem:attention-maxip-minip-threshold-gap}
  With parameters $d=\ell$, $d_{\mathrm{in}}=\ell+1$,
  $d_{\mathrm{out}}=1$, and $m\ge\ell+1$, a single attention unit with input and
  output MLPs solves $\MinIP_{n,\ell,t}$ for $1\le t\le\ell$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:mlp-append, lem:attention-minip-row-formula, lem:attention-minip-yes-gap, lem:attention-minip-no-gap, lem:attention-maxip-minip-threshold-gap}
  Use the same augmented-row input MLP, choose the negative score bilinear form
  $-3\log n\cdot I_{\ell+1}$ and the special row
  $(0,\ldots,0,-(t+1))$.  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-minip-row-formula} gives the
  row formula, Lemmas~\ref{lem:attention-minip-yes-gap} and
  \ref{lem:attention-minip-no-gap} prove the two cases, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-maxip-minip-threshold-gap} supplies the output MLP.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[An attention unit solves Max-IP and Min-IP decision, Theorem C.1]
  \label{thm:attention-solves-maxip-minip}
  \uses{def:transformer, def:tf-solves, def:maxip-dec, def:minip-dec, def:attention-solves-predicate, lem:attention-solves-maxip-dec, lem:attention-solves-minip-dec}
  An attention unit with input and output MLPs and parameters $d = \ell$,
  $d_{\mathrm{in}} = \ell + 1$, $d_{\mathrm{out}} = 1$, $m \ge \ell + 1$ can
  solve $\MaxIP_{n,\ell,t}$ and $\MinIP_{n,\ell,t}$ for $1 \le t \le \ell$; that
  is, $\AttentionSolves{\MaxIP_{n,\ell,t}}$ and
  $\AttentionSolves{\MinIP_{n,\ell,t}}$.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-solves-maxip-dec, lem:attention-solves-minip-dec}
  The Max-IP part is Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-solves-maxip-dec}; the Min-IP
  part is Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-solves-minip-dec}.  Pairing these two
  witnesses gives the combined Theorem C.1 statement.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[MSD threshold zero is solved by a constant MLP]
  \label{lem:attention-msd-zero-threshold}
  \uses{def:msd-dec, def:cosine, def:attention-solves-predicate}
  For nonzero binary inputs, $\MSD_{n,\ell,0}$ is always a yes instance, and a
  constant-output MLP therefore solves this threshold case.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:msd-dec, def:cosine}
  Cosine similarities of nonzero binary vectors lie in $[0,1]$ by
  Definition~\ref{def:cosine}.  Thus every distinct pair has cosine similarity
  at least $0$, so the yes predicate of Definition~\ref{def:msd-dec} holds.
  The output MLP that is constantly $1$ realizes the corresponding solver.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[LSD threshold zero reduces to OV]
  \label{lem:attention-lsd-zero-threshold-ov}
  \uses{def:lsd-dec, def:ov, def:cosine, thm:attention-solves-ov}
  For nonzero binary inputs, the condition
  $\cossim{v_i}{v_j}\le0$ is equivalent to $\inner{v_i}{v_j}=0$.  Hence the
  attention construction for $\OV_{n,\ell}$ solves $\LSD_{n,\ell,0}$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:lsd-dec, def:ov, def:cosine, thm:attention-solves-ov}
  By the binary zero theorem in Definition~\ref{def:cosine}, cosine similarity
  is zero exactly when the inner product is zero; nonnegativity turns
  $\cossim{v_i}{v_j}\le0$ into equality to zero.  Therefore the LSD
  threshold-zero yes predicate is the OV yes predicate, and
  Theorem~\ref{thm:attention-solves-ov} supplies the attention solver.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Normalized MSD transfers to the Max-IP attention construction]
  \label{lem:attention-msd-normalized-maxip-transfer}
  \uses{thm:attention-solves-maxip-minip, lem:mlp-normalize, lem:cosine-normalized-dot, def:msd-dec, def:cosine}
  For $t>0$, after the input MLP maps each nonzero binary row $v_i$ to
  $(v_i/\norm{v_i},1)$ and adds the special row $(0,\ldots,0,t+1)$, the
  $\MSD_{n,\ell,t}$ yes predicate is exactly the Max-IP threshold predicate for
  the normalized rows.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:mlp-normalize, lem:cosine-normalized-dot, def:msd-dec, def:cosine}
  Lemma~\ref{lem:mlp-normalize}, with $\tau=t+1>1$ and $\rho=1$, supplies a
  continuous input MLP producing the normalized augmented rows on the nonzero
  binary domain.  Lemma~\ref{lem:cosine-normalized-dot} identifies each cosine
  similarity with the inner product of the normalized rows.  Thus the MSD
  threshold condition $\cossim{v_i}{v_j}\ge t$ is the same condition used by the
  Max-IP attention analysis on those normalized rows.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Normalized LSD transfers to the Min-IP attention construction]
  \label{lem:attention-lsd-normalized-minip-transfer}
  \uses{thm:attention-solves-maxip-minip, lem:mlp-normalize, lem:cosine-normalized-dot, def:lsd-dec, def:cosine}
  For $t>0$, after the same normalizing input MLP, the
  $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$ yes predicate is exactly the Min-IP threshold predicate for
  the normalized rows.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:mlp-normalize, lem:cosine-normalized-dot, def:lsd-dec, def:cosine}
  The normalizing MLP and cosine-as-normalized-inner-product identity are the
  same as in Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-msd-normalized-maxip-transfer}.  Replacing
  the inequality direction by $\le t$ gives exactly the Min-IP decision
  predicate for the normalized rows, and the negative-score attention
  construction handles that predicate.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[An attention unit solves MSD and LSD decision, Theorem C.2]
  \label{thm:attention-solves-msd-lsd}
  \uses{def:transformer, def:tf-solves, def:msd-dec, def:lsd-dec, def:attention-solves-predicate, lem:attention-msd-zero-threshold, lem:attention-lsd-zero-threshold-ov, lem:attention-msd-normalized-maxip-transfer, lem:attention-lsd-normalized-minip-transfer}
  An attention unit with input and output MLPs and parameters $d = \ell$,
  $d_{\mathrm{in}} = \ell + 1$, $d_{\mathrm{out}} = 1$, $m \ge \ell + 1$ can
  solve $\MSD_{n,\ell,t}$ and $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$ for any $t \in [0,1]$; that is,
  $\AttentionSolves{\MSD_{n,\ell,t}}$ and $\AttentionSolves{\LSD_{n,\ell,t}}$.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:attention-msd-zero-threshold, lem:attention-lsd-zero-threshold-ov, lem:attention-msd-normalized-maxip-transfer, lem:attention-lsd-normalized-minip-transfer, thm:attention-solves-maxip-minip}
  The case $t=0$ for MSD is
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-msd-zero-threshold}; the case $t=0$ for LSD is
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-lsd-zero-threshold-ov}.  For $t>0$,
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-msd-normalized-maxip-transfer} converts MSD to the
  Max-IP attention construction, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:attention-lsd-normalized-minip-transfer} converts LSD to the
  Min-IP attention construction.  The two target constructions are supplied by
  Theorem~\ref{thm:attention-solves-maxip-minip}.
\end{proof}

\chapter{MLP constructions (Appendix D)}

\begin{lemma}[Continuous thresholding MLP, Lemma D.1]
  \label{lem:mlp-threshold}
  \uses{lem:continuous-clipped-affine, lem:clipped-affine-values, lem:continuous-finite-product, lem:finite-product-zero-one}
  For any $a, b \in \R$ with $b > a$, there exists a continuous function
  $f : \R^{\ell} \to \R$ such that
  \[
    f(x) = \begin{cases}
      1 & \text{if } x[i] \ge b \text{ for some } 1 \le i \le \ell,\\
      0 & \text{if } x[i] < a \text{ for all } 1 \le i \le \ell.
    \end{cases}
  \]
  More formally, the existential witness consists of a function $f$, a proof
  that $f$ is continuous, a proof of
  $(\exists i,\ x[i]\ge b)\Rightarrow f(x)=1$, and a proof of
  $(\forall i,\ x[i]<a)\Rightarrow f(x)=0$. Proving only that some continuous
  function exists, for example the constant zero function, omits the behavioral
  guarantees and is not this lemma.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:continuous-clipped-affine, lem:clipped-affine-values, lem:continuous-finite-product, lem:finite-product-zero-one, lem:continuity-closure}
  Define $g : \R \to \R$ by
  \[
    g(y)=\max\!\left(0,\min\!\left(1,\frac{y-a}{b-a}\right)\right).
  \]
  By Lemma~\ref{lem:continuous-clipped-affine}, $g$ is continuous, and by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:clipped-affine-values}, $g(y)=1$ when $y\ge b$ and $g(y)=0$
  when $y<a$. Let
  $f(x)=1-\prod_{i=1}^{\ell}(1-g(x[i]))$. Each coordinate map
  $x\mapsto 1-g(x[i])$ is continuous by composition with the coordinate
  projection and subtraction from a constant, so
  Lemma~\ref{lem:continuous-finite-product} gives continuity of
  $x\mapsto \prod_i(1-g(x[i]))$, and Lemma~\ref{lem:continuity-closure} gives
  continuity of $f$.

  If $x[i_0]\ge b$ for some $i_0$, then $g(x[i_0])=1$, so the $i_0$ factor
  $1-g(x[i_0])$ is $0$. Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-product-zero-one} gives that the
  whole product is $0$, hence $f(x)=1$. If $x[i]<a$ for all $i$, then every
  $g(x[i])=0$, so every factor is $1$; the all-one part of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-product-zero-one} gives that the product is $1$, hence
  $f(x)=0$.

  In Lean, the continuity subproof should be organized as follows. First obtain
  `hg : Continuous g` from Lemma~\ref{lem:continuous-clipped-affine}. Then prove
  the product is continuous using `continuous_finsetProd Finset.univ`; for each
  coordinate $i$, the factor continuity is
  `continuous_const.sub (hg.comp (continuous_apply i))`. Finally close the
  continuity of $f$ by subtracting this product from `continuous_const`.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Continuous coordinate-appending MLP, Lemma D.2]
  \label{lem:mlp-append}
  \uses{lem:continuity-closure}
  For every $\tau>1$, there exists a continuous function
  $f : \R^{\ell} \to \R^{\ell+1}$ such that
  \[
    f(x) = \begin{cases}
      (x, 1) & \text{if } x[\ell] \le 1,\\
      (0, x) & \text{if } x[\ell] \ge \tau.
    \end{cases}
  \]
  The formal witness must include the continuity proof and both regional
  equalities:
  $x[\ell]\le1\Rightarrow f(x)=(x,1)$ and
  $x[\ell]\ge\tau\Rightarrow f(x)=(0,x)$. Equivalently, in coordinate form,
  for all $r\le\ell$:
  \[
    x[\ell]\le1 \Rightarrow
    \bigl(f(x)[r]=x[r]\ (r\le \ell)\ \wedge\ f(x)[\ell+1]=1\bigr),
  \]
  and
  \[
    x[\ell]\ge\tau \Rightarrow
    \bigl(f(x)[1]=0\ \wedge\ f(x)[r+1]=x[r]\ (1\le r\le\ell)\bigr).
  \]
  The proposition carried by this lemma is the conjunction
  \[
    \exists f,\ \operatorname{Continuous}(f)\ \wedge\
    \forall x,\ x[\ell]\le1\Rightarrow f(x)=(x,1)\ \wedge\
    \forall x,\ x[\ell]\ge\tau\Rightarrow f(x)=(0,x).
  \]
  The two implication conclusions are equalities of vectors, not `True'
  placeholders; a constant function cannot witness this lemma.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:continuity-closure}
  Define $g : \R \to \R$ by $g(x) = 1$ if $x \le 1$,
  $g(x) = \frac{\tau-x}{\tau-1}$ if $1 < x < \tau$, and $g(x) = 0$ if
  $x \ge \tau$, which is continuous. Let $f_1(x) = (x, 1)$ and
  $f_2(x) = (0, x)$ in $\R^{\ell+1}$, both continuous. Set
  \[
    f(x) = g(x[\ell])\cdot f_1(x) + (1 - g(x[\ell]))\cdot f_2(x).
  \]
  By Lemma~\ref{lem:continuity-closure}, $f$ is continuous, and one checks
  directly that it equals $(x,1)$ when $x[\ell] \le 1$ and $(0,x)$ when
  $x[\ell] \ge \tau$ (and interpolates continuously in between).
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Continuous normalizing MLP, Lemma D.3]
  \label{lem:mlp-normalize}
  \uses{lem:continuity-closure, lem:mlp-append}
  For every $\tau>1$ and $\rho>0$, there exists a continuous function
  $f : \R^{\ell} \to \R^{\ell+1}$ such that, for every $x$ with
  $\norm{x}\ge \rho$,
  \[
    f(x) = \begin{cases}
      \left(\frac{x}{\norm{x}}, 1\right) & \text{if } x[\ell] \le 1,\\
      \left(0, \frac{x}{\norm{x}}\right) & \text{if } x[\ell] \ge \tau.
    \end{cases}
  \]
  The formal witness must include continuity on all of $\R^\ell$ and the two
  displayed normalization equalities on the restricted domain $\norm{x}\ge\rho$.
  It must therefore construct a safe denominator or equivalent continuous
  extension. In full, the theorem asserts
  \[
    \exists f,\ \operatorname{Continuous}(f)\ \wedge\
    \forall x,\ \norm{x}\ge\rho \Rightarrow
      \left(x[\ell]\le1\Rightarrow
        f(x)=\left(\frac{x}{\norm{x}},1\right)\right)
      \wedge
      \left(x[\ell]\ge\tau\Rightarrow
        f(x)=\left(0,\frac{x}{\norm{x}}\right)\right).
  \]
  The norm lower bound, the two guard conditions, and the two vector equalities
  are all part of the statement. A proof that returns an arbitrary continuous
  function and proves only `True' under the norm hypothesis does not satisfy the
  blueprint node.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:mlp-append, lem:continuity-closure, def:l2norm}
  Let $g$ be the same continuous cutoff as in Lemma~\ref{lem:mlp-append}. Define
  the safe denominator $s_\rho(x)=\max(\norm{x},\rho/2)$, which is continuous and
  strictly positive. Let
  $f_1(x)=\left(\frac{x}{s_\rho(x)},1\right)$ and
  $f_2(x)=\left(0,\frac{x}{s_\rho(x)}\right)$, both continuous on all of
  $\R^\ell$. Then
  \[
    f(x) = g(x[\ell])\cdot f_1(x) + (1 - g(x[\ell]))\cdot f_2(x)
  \]
  is continuous by Lemma~\ref{lem:continuity-closure}. On inputs with
  $\norm{x}\ge\rho$, the safe denominator equals $\norm{x}$; if in addition
  $x[\ell]\le 1$ then $g(x[\ell])=1$, and if $x[\ell]\ge\tau$ then
  $g(x[\ell])=0$. Hence the required piecewise values hold on the separated
  nonzero input region used by the construction.
\end{proof}
